Causes of Termination of Lease: Defects and Physical Ruin
Explaining that lease is terminated by defect, house collapse, and water cut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a lease may be terminated due to a defect or physical ruin, and distinguish between harmful and non-harmful defects according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A lease is not automatically terminated by a defect; it requires an act of termination or court order.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq opens the chapter on termination of lease (فسخ الإجارة). It addresses the legal effect of defects and physical ruin on the lease contract. The key Hanafi principle is that the lease is not automatically dissolved; rather, the lessee or the judge must effect termination. The text also distinguishes between defects that harm the intended benefit (giving the right to terminate) and those that do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Recognize that the title indicates the lease 'is terminated by defect.' The apparent wording suggests automaticity, but the text immediately qualifies.
The author uses 'تفسخ' which is ambiguous.
2
Analyze the intra-school dispute
Examine the differing views: some say termination is automatic; the majority (and correct view) require an act of termination or court order.
The tarjih is based on al-Ziyadat and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Distinguish harmful vs. non-harmful defects
Note that only defects that harm the intended benefit give the right to terminate. Minor defects do not affect the contract's binding nature.
Examples from al-Bada'i': slave losing one eye (non-harmful) vs. falling ill (harmful).
4
Identify conditions for termination
Termination is only valid if the lessor is present or, if absent, the matter is referred to a judge. The lessee cannot unilaterally terminate.
The lessee's continued use after the defect means he owes full rent.
5
Note the specific causes mentioned
The passage introduces 'ruin of the house' and 'cut-off of water for the mill' as specific grounds, though the discussion is cut off.
These are examples of physical circumstances that make the leased property unusable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فسخ الإجارة
ذكر الفسخ آخراً لأن فسخ العقد بعد وجوده لا محالة فناسب ذكره آخراً. قال رحمه
الله : ( وتفسخ بالعيب أي تفسخ الإجارة بالعيب، وظاهر قوله وظاهر قوله «تفسخ» أفاد أنها لا تتوقف على رضا الآخر ولا على القضاء وفي التتارخانية : وإذا تحقق العذر هل ينفسخ بنفسه أو يحتاج إلى الفسخ ؟ إشارات الكتب متعارضة ففي بعضها ينفسخ بنفس العذر أخذ و به هو بعض المشايخ وفي عامتها يحتاج إلى الفسخ وعليه عامة المشايخ وهو الصحيح، وقيل العقد ينفسخ بدون الرضا قيل هو الصحيح وبعض المشايخ قال : إن كان العذر يمنع المضي ينفسخ بنفسه ولا يحتاج إلى القضاء، وإن كان لا يمنع المضي يحتاج إلى القضاء اهـ . وفي الزيادات: يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفسخ الإجارة. قال شمس الأئمة: رواية الزيادات أصح ؛ ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي الجامع الصغير : يشترط لصحة الفسخ الرضا أو القضاء اهـ . وأطلق المؤلف في العيب وقال في البدائع : هذا إذا كان العيب مما يضر بالانتفاع بالمستأجر، فإن زمان لا يضر بالانتفاع به بقي العقد لازماً ولا خيار للمستأجر كالعبد المستأجر ذهبت إحدى عينيه وذلك لا يضر بالخدمة أو سقط شعره أو سقط في الدار المستأجرة حائط لا ينتفع به في سكناها إلى آخره بخلاف ما إذا كان العيب الحادث مما يضر بالانتفاع لأنه إذا كان يضر بالانتفاع فالنقصان إلى المعقود عليه فأوجب له الخيار فله أن يفسخ، ثم إنما يلي الفسخ يرجع إذا كان المؤجر حاضراً، فإن كان غائباً فحدت بالمستأجر ما يوجب حق الفسخ فليس للمستأجر أن يفسخ لأن فسخ العقد لا يجوز إلا بحضور العاقدين أو من يقوم مقامهما، فلو كان لا يضر بها فليس له الفسخ كالعبد المستأجر إذا ذهب إحدى عينيه وهي لا تضر بالخدمة أو الدار إذا سقط منها حائط لا ينتفع به في سكناها وإن كان يؤثر في السكنى أو الخدمة كالعبد إذا مرض أو الدابة إذا دبرت أو الدار إذا سقط منها حائط ينتفع به في السكنى. ولو استأجر دارین فسقط من أحدهما حائط أو منع مانع من أحدهما أو وجد في أحدهما عيب ينقص السكنى فله أن يتركهما جميعاً إذا كان عقد عليهما عقد واحد. اهـ. قال الشارح: لأن العقد يقتضي سلامة البدل فإذا لم يسلم فات رضاه فله أن يفسخ كما في البيع. والمعقود عليه هنا المنافع وهي تحدث ساعة فساعة فما وجد من العيب يكون حادثاً قبل القبض في حق ما بقي من المنافع فيوجب خيار الفسخ فإذا فعل المؤجر ما زال به العيب فلا خيار للمستأجر لأن الموجب للرد قد زال قبل الفسخ والعقد يتجدد ساعة فساعة فلم يوجد فيما يأتي بعد فسقط اختيار الفسخ ، وإذا استوفى المستأجر المنفعة مع العيب يلزمه جميع البدل. وفي الظهيرية : وذلك إما أن يكون من قبل أحد العاقدين أو من قبل المعقود عليه. وفي التجريد : إما أن يمنع الانتفاع أو ينقص الانتفاع بالمنفعة. ولما تنوع العيب إلى هذه الأنواع شرع يبين الأنواع .
قال
رحمه الله : (وخراب الدار وانقطاع ماء الضيغة والرحى) يعني تنفسخ الإجارة بهذه الأشياء ولو بين المؤجر الدار وأراد المستأجر أن يسكنه في بقية المدة فليس له أن يمنعه من
Chapter on the Termination of Lease. He mentioned termination last because the termination of a contract after its existence is inevitable, so it was appropriate to mention it last. He (the author) said: (And it is terminated by defect) meaning the lease is terminated by defect. The apparent meaning of his saying 'is terminated' indicates that it does not depend on the consent of the other nor on a court order. In al-TatarKhaniyya: 'When an excuse is realized, does it terminate by itself or does it need termination? The indications in the books are contradictory. In some, it terminates by the excuse itself, and that is taken by some scholars. In most, it needs termination, and that is the view of the majority of scholars, and it is correct. And it is said that the contract terminates without consent; it is said that is correct. Some scholars said: If the excuse prevents continuation, it terminates by itself and does not need the court; if it does not prevent continuation, it needs the court.' End. In al-Ziyadat: 'The matter is referred to the judge to terminate the lease.' Shams al-A'immah said: 'The narration of al-Ziyadat is more correct.' Thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'For the validity of termination, consent or court order is required.' End. The author left the term 'defect' absolute. In al-Bada'i': 'This is when the defect harms the lessee's benefit. If it does not harm the benefit, the contract remains binding and the lessee has no option, like a hired slave who loses one eye which does not harm the service, or his hair falls out, or in a rented house a wall falls that is not needed for living in it, etc. Contrary to when the defect harms the benefit, because if it harms the benefit, there is a deficiency in what was contracted for, so it gives him the option; he may terminate. Then, he has the right to terminate only when the lessor is present. If the lessor is absent, and a cause for termination occurs to the lessee, the lessee may not terminate because termination of a contract is not valid except in the presence of the two contracting parties or their representatives. If it does not harm, he has no termination, like a hired slave who loses one eye which does not harm the service, or a house from which a wall falls that is not needed for living in it. But if it affects the living or service, like a slave who falls ill, or an animal that is injured, or a house from which a wall falls that is needed for living, then he may terminate. If one rents two houses and a wall falls from one, or a hindrance occurs in one, or a defect is found in one that diminishes the living, he may leave both if they were contracted in one contract.' End. The commentator said: 'Because the contract requires the soundness of the substitute. If it is not sound, his consent is lost, so he may terminate as in sale. Here, the subject matter is benefits, which arise moment by moment. Any defect that occurs before delivery with respect to the remaining benefits gives the option to terminate. If the lessor does something that removes the defect, the lessee has no option, because the cause for return has ceased before termination, and the contract is renewed moment by moment, so no defect exists thereafter, so the option falls. If the lessee enjoys the benefit despite the defect, he owes the entire rent.' In al-Zahiriyya: 'That is either from one of the contracting parties or from the subject matter.' In al-Tajrid: 'Either prevents the benefit or diminishes the benefit.' Since the defect is of these types, he began to explain the types. He (the author) said: (And the ruin of the house, and the cut-off of water for the mill, and the mill itself) meaning the lease is terminated by these things, even if the lessor offers another house and the lessee wants to live in it for the remainder of the term, he (the lessor) cannot prevent him from...
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on termination of lease (فسخ الإجارة). It first discusses the general rule that lease is terminated by defects. The text notes a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: some say termination is automatic upon occurrence of the defect, while the majority (and the correct view) hold that it requires an act of termination by the lessee or a court order. The text then specifies that only defects that harm the intended benefit give the right to terminate; minor defects do not. It also discusses conditions for termination, such as the presence of the lessor. The passage then moves to specific causes: ruin of the house, cut-off of water for the mill, and the mill itself. The text is cut off at the end of the page.

Key Terms
فسخ الإجارة (faskh al-ijāra): Termination of the lease contract before its natural expiry due to a legal cause
العيب (al-‘ayb): A defect in the leased property that diminishes the intended benefit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, does a lease terminate automatically upon the occurrence of a defect?
A) Yes, immediately
B) Yes, but only after three days
C) No, it requires an act of termination
D) No, it never terminates

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, lease termination due to a defect requires an act of termination; it is not automatic, and only defects that harm the benefit give the right to terminate.

Dissolution of Lease Due to Defect: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the general ruling on dissolving lease for defects, including intra-Hanafi dispute on procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a lease dissolves due to a defect and distinguish between the positions on whether dissolution requires a court order or consent.

Core Idea
Only defects that harm the benefit give the option to dissolve; dissolution requires an act, not automatic.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the general dissolution of a lease due to a defect. The matn suggests automatic dissolution, but the commentary reveals a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: does dissolution require a court or consent? We'll unpack the conditions and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling condition
Determine when a defect gives the option to dissolve. The text states only defects that harm the benefit to the lessee trigger the option.
Examples: losing an eye that does not affect service does not harm benefit.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some mashayikh say dissolution is automatic upon a defect that prevents continuation. The majority require an act of dissolution (court or consent). A third view distinguishes: if defect prevents continuation, automatic; otherwise court needed.
The dispute is about procedure, not the existence of the option.
3
Locate the preferred narration
Al-Ziyadat reports raising the matter to the judge. Shams al-A'imma declares this narration more correct. Al-Jami' al-Saghir requires consent or court.
This establishes the mufta bihi: dissolution requires an act.
4
Apply the principle to examples
If defect harms benefit (e.g., sick slave, collapsed wall needed for dwelling), option exists. If not (e.g., lost eye but still serves), no option. Dissolution must be effected with consent or court.
Presence of both parties or representatives is required for valid dissolution.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
If dissolution is an act, rent continues until dissolution is performed. If automatic, rent stops immediately upon defect.
This difference affects the lessee's financial obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفسخ بالعيب أي تفسخ الإجارة بالعيب، وظاهر قوله «تفسخ» أفاد أنها لا تتوقف على رضا الآخر ولا على القضاء وفي التتارخانية : وإذا تحقق العذر هل ينفسخ بنفسه أو يحتاج إلى الفسخ ؟ إشارات الكتب متعارضة ففي بعضها ينفسخ بنفس العذر وبه أخذ بعض المشايخ وفي عامتها يحتاج إلى الفسخ وعليه عامة المشايخ وهو الصحيح، وقيل العقد ينفسخ بدون الرضا قيل هو الصحيح وبعض المشايخ قال : إن كان العذر يمنع المضي ينفسخ بنفسه ولا يحتاج إلى القضاء، وإن كان لا يمنع المضي يحتاج إلى القضاء اهـ . وفي الزيادات: يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفسخ الإجارة. قال شمس الأئمة: رواية الزيادات أصح ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي الجامع الصغير : يشترط لصحة الفسخ الرضا أو القضاء اهـ . وأطلق المؤلف في العيب وقال في البدائع : هذا إذا كان العيب مما يضر بالانتفاع بالمستأجر، فإن كان لا يضر بالانتفاع به بقي العقد لازماً ولا خيار للمستأجر كالعبد المستأجر ذهبت إحدى عينيه وذلك لا يضر بالخدمة أو سقط شعره أو سقط في الدار المستأجرة حائط لا ينتفع به في سكناها إلى آخره بخلاف ما إذا كان العيب الحادث مما يضر بالانتفاع لأنه إذا كان يضر بالانتفاع فالنقصان إلى المعقود عليه فأوجب له الخيار فله أن يفسخ، ثم إنما يلي الفسخ يرجع إذا كان المؤجر حاضراً، فإن كان غائباً فحدث بالمستأجر ما يوجب حق الفسخ فليس للمستأجر أن يفسخ لأن فسخ العقد لا يجوز إلا بحضور العاقدين أو من يقوم مقامهما، فلو كان لا يضر بالانتفاع فليس له الفسخ كالعبد المستأجر إذا ذهب إحدى عينيه وهي لا تضر بالخدمة أو الدار إذا سقط منها حائط لا ينتفع به في سكناها وإن كان يؤثر في السكنى أو الخدمة كالعبد إذا مرض أو الدابة إذا دبرت أو الدار إذا سقط منها حائط ينتفع به في السكنى. ولو استأجر دارین فسقط من أحدهما حائط أو منع مانع من أحدهما أو وجد في أحدهما عيب ينقص السكنى فله أن يتركهما جميعاً إذا كان عقد عليهما عقد واحد. اهـ. قال الشارح: لأن العقد يقتضي سلامة البدل فإذا لم يسلم فات رضاه فله أن يفسخ كما في البيع. والمعقود عليه هنا المنافع وهي تحدث ساعة فساعة فما وجد من العيب يكون حادثاً قبل القبض في حق ما بقي من المنافع فيوجب خيار الفسخ فإذا فعل المؤجر ما زال به العيب فلا خيار للمستأجر لأن الموجب للرد قد زال قبل الفسخ والعقد يتجدد ساعة فساعة فلم يوجد فيما يأتي بعد فسقط اختيار الفسخ ، وإذا استوفى المستأجر المنفعة مع العيب يلزمه جميع البدل. وفي الظهيرية : وذلك إما أن يكون من قبل أحد العاقدين أو من قبل المعقود عليه. وفي التجريد : إما أن يمنع الانتفاع أو ينقص الانتفاع بالمنفعة. ولما تنوع العيب إلى هذه الأنواع شرع يبين الأنواع .
And it dissolves due to defect, i.e., the lease dissolves due to defect. The apparent meaning of his statement 'dissolves' indicates that it does not depend on the consent of the other nor on a court order. And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: 'When the excuse is realized, does it dissolve by itself or does it require dissolution? The references in the books conflict. In some, it dissolves by the mere excuse, and some mashayikh adopted this. In most of them, it requires dissolution, and upon this are the generality of the mashayikh, and it is the correct view. And it has been said that the contract dissolves without consent, and it has been said this is correct. And some mashayikh said: If the excuse prevents continuation, it dissolves by itself and does not need a court order; if it does not prevent continuation, it needs a court order.' And in al-Ziyadat: 'The matter is raised to the judge to dissolve the lease.' Shams al-A'imma said: 'The narration of al-Ziyadat is more correct.' Likewise in al-Khulasa. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'For the validity of dissolution, consent or a court order is required.' The author said generally about the defect, and it is said in al-Bada'i': 'This is if the defect harms the benefit to the lessee. If it does not harm the benefit, the contract remains binding and there is no option for the lessee, like a hired slave who loses one eye, but that does not harm the service, or his hair falls out, or a wall in the hired house collapses that is not used for dwelling, etc. Contrary to if the newly occurring defect harms the benefit, because if it harms the benefit, the deficiency relates to the subject matter, so it gives him the option, so he may dissolve. Then the dissolution is only valid if the lessor is present. If he is absent and something occurs to the lessee that gives him the right to dissolve, the lessee may not dissolve because dissolving the contract is not permitted except in the presence of the two contracting parties or their representatives. If it does not harm the benefit, he has no right to dissolve, like a hired slave who loses one eye and that does not harm the service, or a house from which a wall falls that is not used for dwelling, even if it affects the dwelling or service, like a slave who becomes ill, or an animal that becomes exhausted, or a house from which a wall falls that is used for dwelling. If one leases two houses and a wall collapses in one, or an impediment prevents use of one, or a defect reducing dwelling is found in one, he may leave both if the contract was a single contract for both.' The commentator said: 'Because the contract requires the integrity of the substitute. If it is not sound, his consent is lost, so he may dissolve as in sale. And the subject matter here is the benefits, which occur moment by moment. So whatever defect occurs is a pre-existing defect before delivery with respect to the remaining benefits, so it gives the option to dissolve. If the lessor does something that removes the defect, then there is no option for the lessee because the cause for return has been removed before dissolution, and the contract is renewed moment by moment, so it does not exist in the future, so the option to dissolve falls. If the lessee enjoys the benefit despite the defect, the full rent is due from him.' And in al-Zahiriyyah: 'That is either from one of the two contracting parties or from the subject matter.' And in al-Tajrid: 'Either it prevents the benefit or reduces the benefit.' Since the defect varies into these types, the author proceeds to explain the types.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the dissolution of a lease contract due to a defect in the subject matter. The commentator begins by clarifying the apparent meaning of the matn which states that the lease dissolves due to a defect, indicating that dissolution does not require the consent of the other party or a court order. However, he immediately presents an intra-Hanafi dispute from al-Tatar Khaniyyah: when an excuse (like a defect) is realized, does the contract dissolve automatically or does it require an act of dissolution? Some books say it dissolves by itself, and some mashayikh adopted this. But the majority hold that dissolution requires an explicit act, and this is the correct view. A third position distinguishes: if the excuse prevents continuation of the contract, it dissolves automatically without court intervention; if it does not prevent continuation, court intervention is needed. The text then cites al-Ziyadat that the matter must be raised to the judge, and Shams al-A'imma deems that narration more correct. Al-Jami' al-Saghir requires consent or a court order for valid dissolution. The commentator then explains that the matn's general statement about defects is qualified: only defects that harm the lessee's benefit give the right to dissolve. If the defect does not harm the benefit, the contract remains binding. Examples: a hired slave losing an eye does not harm service, so no option; a wall collapsing that does not affect dwelling similarly. Conversely, if the defect harms the benefit (e.g., a slave falling ill, an animal becoming exhausted, a wall needed for dwelling), the lessee has the option to dissolve. The commentator also notes that dissolution can only be effected in the presence of both parties or their representatives; if the lessor is absent, the lessee cannot unilaterally dissolve. A special case: if two houses are leased together and one becomes defective, the lessee may cancel both if the contract was single. The commentator provides the reasoning: the contract requires the subject matter to be sound; if unsound, consent is vitiated, analogous to sale (qiyas). Benefits arise moment by moment, so a defect occurring before delivery for remaining benefits gives the option. If the lessor remedies the defect before dissolution, the option falls because the contract renews each moment. If the lessee uses the item despite the defect, full rent is due. The passage concludes by noting the classification of defects: from one party or the subject matter, and whether they prevent or reduce benefit. This sets the stage for the specific examples that follow.

Key Terms
فسخ الإجارة (faskh al-ijarah): Dissolution of a lease contract due to a defect or other excuse.
عيب حادث (ayb hadith): A defect that arises after the contract is concluded but before or during the lease term.
خيار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): The option to dissolve the contract, granted to the lessee if a defect harms the benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person hires a slave to carry goods, and the slave loses one eye but can still carry. Does the lessee have the option to dissolve the lease?
A) Yes, because any defect gives the option.
B) No, because the defect does not harm the agreed benefit.
C) Yes, but only if the lessor is present.
D) No, because the lessee must accept the slave as is.

Key Takeaway
Only defects that harm the benefit give the option to dissolve, and dissolution requires an act (court/consent), not automation.

Specific Defects Causing Lease Dissolution: House Collapse and Water Cutoff
Expands on specific excuses for lease dissolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific defects in an ijara contract that give the right to dissolve, apply the condition of proportional rent when partial benefit remains, and distinguish between excessive and non-excessive decrease in mill capacity.

Core Idea
Collapse and water cutoff dissolve the lease; but if some benefit remains, pay proportionally.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on specific defects that justify dissolution of an ijara (lease) contract. The Hanafi school recognizes that certain external events, such as the collapse of a leased house or the cutoff of water supply for a farm or mill, destroy the intended benefit and thereby give the lessee the right to terminate. However, if some use remains (e.g., a mill building usable for storage), rent is reduced proportionally. The passage also addresses intra-madhhab differences on whether water cutoff of a mill dissolves the lease and what constitutes an excessive decrease in grinding capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defects and their rulings
List the three specific defects mentioned: house collapse, water cutoff of a farm (day'a), and water cutoff of a mill (raha). For each, determine whether the lease dissolves entirely or conditionally.
House collapse: lease dissolves. Water cutoff of farm: lease dissolves. Water cutoff of mill: disputed (some say dissolves, others say not).
2
Apply the principle of proportional rent
When the subject matter partially survives (e.g., mill building remains useful for storage), the lessee owes rent proportional to the remaining benefit. Identify the condition: 'if something remains that can be used for other than grinding, then he owes rent in proportion.'
This is based on the Hanafi rule that rent is for benefit (manfa'a); if part of the benefit remains, rent is due for that part.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on mill water cutoff
Contrast the majority view (al-Nawadir: dissolution permitted) with the view in al-Dhakhira (lease does not dissolve). Note the practical consequence: under al-Dhakhira, the lessee must continue paying full rent despite the water cutoff.
The text presents both positions; the mufta bihi is not explicitly stated, but the passage overall leans toward dissolution as the standard.
4
Distinguish between excessive and non-excessive decrease for mills
For mills, a mere decrease in capacity does not dissolve the lease unless the decrease is 'excessive' (fahish). Apply al-Quduri's definition: 'if grinding becomes less than half of what it was', then it is excessive and gives the right to dissolve.
This quantitative threshold prevents frivolous dissolution.
5
Apply analogous cases from the text
Consider the examples given: a dismantled and reassembled ship cannot be delivered to the lessee; flooding, salinization, or swampiness of land are excuses; if a crop perishes, the lessee may replant a similar or less harmful crop or dissolve. Use these to test your understanding of the underlying principle: loss of intended benefit.
These analogies reinforce that the right to dissolve arises when the core benefit is destroyed.

قال رحمه الله : (وخراب الدار وانقطاع ماء الضيعة والرحى) يعني تنفسخ الإجارة بهذه الأشياء ولو بين المؤجر الدار وأراد المستأجر أن يسكنه في بقية المدة فليس له أن يمنع من ذلك، وكذا ليس للمستأجر أن يمنع منه . وفي النوادر : بنى المؤجر الدار كلها قبل الفسخ فللمستأجر أن يفسخ العقد إن شاء وهو مخالف لما تقدم، ولو انقطع ماء الرحى والبيت وبقي ما ينتفع به لغير الطحن فعليه من الأجر بحصته لأنه بقي شيء من المعقود عليه إذا استوفاه لزمه حصته. وقوله وخراب الدار إلى آخره يفيد أن الإجارة تنفسخ بهذه الأشياء. وفي الذخيرة: الإجارة في الرحى لا تنفسخ بانقطاع وفي الخانية : فإن بني الدار بعد الفسخ فليس للمستأجر أن يسكنها . وفي التتارخانية : والسفينة المستأجرة إذا نقضت وصارت ألواحاً ثم أعيدت سفينة أخرى لم يجز تسليمها للمستأجر .اهـ. ومثل انقطاع ماء الرحى الحجر. وفي التتارخانية : ولو استأجره ليزرع أرضه ببذره ثم بدا له أن لا يزرع كان عذراً، ولو استأجر أرضاً ليزرعها فغرقت أو تربت أو سبخت كان ذلك عذراً في فسخها. وفي الأصل: استأجر أرضاً ليزرعها شيئاً سماه فزرعها ذلك وأصاب الزرع آفة وذهب وفت الزراعة لذلك الزرع فأراد أن يزرع ما هو أقل منه ضرراً أو مثله فله ذلك وإلا فسخت ولزمه ما مضى من الأجرة قيد بانقطاع الرحى ليحترز عن النقصان في الرحا، فإن كان النقصان فاحشاً فله حق الفسخ ، وإن كان غير فاحش فليس له حق الفسخ. قال القدوري : إذا صار الطحن أقل من نصف الحنطة أو لا فهو فاحش
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And the collapse of the house, and the cutoff of water of the farm and the mill.' Means the lease dissolves due to these things. Even if the lessor repairs the house and the lessee wants to inhabit it for the remaining period, the lessor cannot prevent him, and likewise the lessee cannot prevent him. And in al-Nawadir: 'The lessor built the entire house before dissolution, so the lessee may dissolve the contract if he wishes, and this contradicts what preceded.' And if the water of the mill and the house is cut off, but something remains that can be used for other than grinding, then he owes rent in proportion to that because something of the subject matter remains; if he uses it, he owes its proportion. His statement 'and the collapse of the house' etc. indicates that the lease dissolves due to these things. And in al-Dhakhira: 'The lease of a mill does not dissolve upon the cutoff of water.' And in al-Khaniyyah: 'If the house is built after dissolution, the lessee may not inhabit it.' And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: 'A leased ship, if it is dismantled and becomes planks, then remade into another ship, it is not permitted to deliver it to the lessee.' Similarly to the cutoff of mill water is the stone. And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: 'If one hires him to cultivate his land with his own seed, then it occurs to him not to cultivate, that is an excuse. And if one leases land to cultivate and it is flooded, or becomes saline, or becomes swampy, that is an excuse for dissolution.' And in al-Asl: 'One leased land to cultivate a specified crop, he cultivated it, then a blight struck the crop and it perished, and the farming for that crop was finished; so he wanted to plant a less harmful or similar crop, he may do so; otherwise the lease is dissolved and he owes the rent for what has passed.' The restriction to the cutoff of the mill is to distinguish from a decrease in the mill. If the decrease is excessive, he has the right to dissolve; if not excessive, he does not. Al-Quduri said: 'If the grinding becomes less than half of what it was, or less, it is excessive.'
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn, providing specific examples of defects that cause lease dissolution: the collapse of a house, cutoff of water for a farm or mill. The commentator explains that if the house collapses, the lease dissolves. Even if the lessor rebuilds the house before the lessee dissolves the contract, the lessee still has the option to dissolve, according to al-Nawadir, though this is contradictory to what was previously mentioned (that rebuilding removes the option). If water is cut off for mill and house, but some benefit remains (e.g., house can still be lived in), then the lessee owes rent proportional to the remaining benefit. The commentator cites several sources: al-Dhakhira says the lease of a mill does not dissolve due to water cutoff; al-Khaniyyah says if the house is rebuilt after dissolution, the lessee cannot inhabit it; al-Tatar Khaniyyah discusses a ship dismantled and reassembled—cannot be delivered. For a stone (like a millstone) it is similar to water cutoff. Excuses for land lease: if the lessee decides not to cultivate (without external cause), that is an excuse; flooding, salinization, or swampiness are excuses. If a crop perishes, the lessee may replant with a less harmful or similar crop; otherwise the lease is dissolved and rent is due for the past period. The passage concludes with a distinction for mills: a decrease in grinding capacity must be excessive to give the right to dissolve. Al-Quduri defines excessive as when grinding output becomes less than half of the normal.

Key Terms
خراب الدار (kharab al-dar): Collapse or destruction of the leased house, making it uninhabitable.
انقطاع ماء الضيعة (inqita' ma' al-day'a): Cutoff of water supply for an irrigated farm, rendering cultivation impossible.
فاحش (fahish): Excessive; a decrease in mill grinding capacity to less than half of normal, giving right to dissolve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Defects that destroy the primary benefit of a lease (house collapse, water cutoff, excessive mill decrease) give the lessee the right to dissolve, with proportional rent adjustment if partial benefit remains.

Lease Dissolution Upon Death of a Party
Ruling on lease dissolution upon death of lessor or lessee, with Shafi'i dispute and response, and procedural methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lease dissolution upon death of a party and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, applying the necessity exception.

Core Idea
Death dissolves a lease moment-by-moment unless necessity dictates continuation.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute: does a lease contract end when the lessor or lessee dies? The Hanafi school holds that it does, because the contract renews moment by moment. The Shafi'i school disagrees. We will explore the Hanafi proof, an objection from practice, and the necessity-based exception that reconciles apparent inconsistencies.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its condition
Identify that the lease dissolves upon death only if the party contracted for themselves (not as an agent or guardian). Note the indication that no court order is needed.
The phrase 'عقدها لنفسه' is key: if for another, no dissolution.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that death does not nullify the lease; the contract continues binding on the heirs.
The text does not quote Shafi'i's proof, only the ruling.
3
Follow the Hanafi rational dalil
The lease is a continuous transfer of benefits moment by moment. The lessor's death severs ownership of future benefits, so the contract cannot continue.
Reasoning is dalil aqli; the text provides the Arabic: 'العقد ينعقد ساعة فساعة'.
4
Analyze the objection and Hanafi response
The counterexample of a hirer stranded in the desert continuing after the owner's death is answered by necessity. If no alternative mount or judge, continuation is permitted; otherwise dissolution.
This shows the principle is not absolute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practically, Hanafi heirs cannot demand rent after death (unless necessity); Shafi'i heirs become lessors. The Hanafi position is upheld with the necessity exception.
Also an intra-Hanafi procedural difference: automatic dissolution vs. court order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتعاقدين إن عقدها لنفسه وإن عقدها لغيره لا كالوكيل والوصي والمتولي في الوقف. قال رحمه الله : ( وتفسخ بموت أحد عقدها لنفسه) قال الشارح : وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يحتاج إلى حكم الحاكم ا هـ . والظاهر أن فيه إشارة إليه قال في المفيد والمزيد وقال بعضهم لا لكن يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ويقضي بالفسخ ولا يحتاج في ذلك إلى دعوى وللعلماء في ذلك طريقان: أحدهما أن يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي بالفسخ. الثانية أن يبيع العين المؤجرة ويحكم القاضي فيها بالصحة وانفساخ الأولى وهي طريقة ما وراء النهر. وقال الشافعي: لا تبطل بموت أحدهما. ولنا أن العقد ينعقد ساعة فساعة حسب حدوث المنفعة فإذا مات المؤجر انتقل الملك إلى الوارث ومنفعته إليه والمنافع المستحقة بالعقد هي المملوكة للمؤجر وقد فات بموته فتنفسخ . قال في العتابية : ونوقض بما إذا استأجر دابة إلى مكان معين فمات صاحب الدابة وسط الطريق كان للمستأجر أن يركبها إلى المكان المسمى وقد مات أحدهما أو عقدها لنفسه. وأجبت بأن ذلك للضرورة وأنه يخاف على نفسه وماله حيث لا يجدد دابة أخرى في وسط المفازة ولا يكون ثمة قاض يرفع الأمر إليه حتى قال بعض مشايخنا : إن وجد ثمة دابة أخرى يحمل عليها متاعه ينتقض أو وجد قاض ينتقض ا.هـ. وفي المحيط : إذا مات رب الدابة نظر القاضي ما هو الأصلح للورثة؛ إن رأى بيع الجمل وحفظ الثمن أنفع للورثة ،فعل، وإن رأى إبقاء الإجارة فإن كان بقية فالأفضل الإبقاء، وإن كان غير بقية والأفضل فسخها، فإن فسخها وأقام البينة أنه أوفاه الكراء رد عليه بحساب ما بقي ولو أنفق المستأجر على الدابة شيئاً لم يحسب له إلا
The two contracting parties: if he made the contract for himself, [it dissolves]; if he made it for another, it does not, like the agent, executor, and administrator of a waqf. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And it dissolves upon the death of one of the two, if he made the contract for himself.' The commentator said: 'In this is an indication that it does not need a ruling of the judge.' And it appears that there is an indication of that. It is said in al-Mufid and al-Mazid: 'And some said no, but the matter is raised to the judge and he decides on the dissolution, and there is no need for a claim in that. The scholars have two ways: one is to raise the matter to the judge for dissolution. The second is to sell the leased property and the judge rules on its validity and the dissolution of the first contract; this is the method of Transoxiana.' Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'It does not become void by the death of one of the two.' And for us (Hanafis): the contract is concluded moment by moment according to the occurrence of the benefit. So if the lessor dies, ownership transfers to the heir, and his benefit goes to him, while the benefits due by contract were owned by the lessor and have been lost by his death, so it dissolves. It is said in al-Utabiyyah: 'It was objected by the case of one who hires an animal to a specific place, and the owner of the animal dies in the middle of the road; the lessee may ride it to the named place, even though one of them has died or he made the contract for himself.' The answer is that this is due to necessity, and he fears for himself and his property because there is no other animal in the middle of the desert and no judge to raise the matter to. Some of our mashayikh even said: 'If there is another animal there to carry his goods, the objection would hold, or if there is a judge, it would hold.' In al-Muhit: 'When the owner of the animal dies, the judge considers what is best for the heirs. If he sees that selling the camel and preserving the price is more beneficial for the heirs, he does so. If he sees keeping the lease, if there is a remaining period, keeping it is better; if there is no remaining period and dissolving is better, he dissolves it. If he dissolves it and the lessee proves that he paid the rent, the rent is refunded in proportion to what remains. And if the lessee spent anything on the animal, it is not credited to him except...'
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether a lease contract dissolves upon the death of one of the parties. According to the Hanafi school, if the contract was made by the party for their own benefit (not as an agent or guardian), the lease dissolves upon their death. The matn states that it dissolves, and the commentator notes that this implies no court order is needed. However, a second opinion requires raising the matter to the judge for dissolution, and a third method in Transoxiana involves selling the leased item and the judge confirming the dissolution. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that death does not nullify the lease. The Hanafi proof is rational: the contract is renewed moment by moment as benefits are generated. When the lessor dies, ownership of the benefits that were due passes to the heir, but those benefits were owned by the lessor only moment by moment; his death cuts off that ownership, so the contract terminates. An objection is raised: if someone hires a mount to a destination and the owner dies en route, the Hanafis permit the hirer to continue to the destination despite the death. How is this consistent? The answer is necessity: the hirer is stranded and cannot easily get another mount or a judge. If another mount or a judge were available, the contract would dissolve. The passage then discusses the judge's role in determining the best course for the heirs after the death of the lessor: either selling the property or continuing the lease if beneficial. If the lease is dissolved, the lessee gets a refund for the unused portion. Expenses incurred by the lessee on the animal are not reimbursed (sentence incomplete).

Key Terms
موت أحد المتعاقدين (mawt ahad al-muta'aqidayn): Death of one of the two contracting parties (lessor or lessee) in a lease.
عقدها لنفسه ('aqadaha li nafsihi): The party entered the contract for their own benefit, not as a representative for another.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity; used to justify the exception when a lessee continues to use the hired animal after the owner's death due to lack of alternatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a camel to carry goods to a distant market. During the journey, the camel's owner dies. There is no other transport and no judge nearby. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling?
A) The lease dissolves immediately, and the man must return the camel.
B) The man may continue to use the camel to reach the destination due to necessity.
C) The man must find a judge to dissolve the lease.
D) The man must pay the rent to the owner's heirs but cannot continue.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a lease entered for oneself dissolves upon the death of a party due to the moment-by-moment nature of the contract, except when necessity forces continuation.

Excuses (A'dhar) for Terminating a Lease
Compilation of Hanafi rulings on termination of ijarah due to excuses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid excuses for terminating an ijarah and apply the egregious deficiency (fāḥish) threshold as defined by al-Quduri.

Core Idea
A lease may only be terminated if the defect is egregious (fāḥish), i.e., reduces utility by more than half.

This passage compiles various Hanafi rulings on when a lessee may terminate a lease due to unforeseen events. The overarching principle is that not every defect justifies termination; only an egregious deficiency—defined by al-Quduri as a reduction to less than half of normal function—gives the right to rescind. Additionally, if some benefit remains, the lessee must pay rent proportionately for the period of use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of excuses
List the specific excuses mentioned: stoppage of water for a mill, destruction of the house, flooding or salinization of land, change of mind by the farmer, blight destroying the crop, and dismantling of a leased ship.
Each excuse is treated differently depending on whether the lessee can still derive some benefit.
2
Determine the legal consequence for each excuse
For each excuse, note whether the lease is terminated or only reduced proportionately. For example, if water stops but the building can be used for other purposes, rent is reduced pro rata.
The text explicitly states when termination is allowed and when only a rent reduction applies.
3
Extract the general rule: egregious deficiency
The passage concludes with al-Quduri's definition: if the grinding capacity becomes less than half of the normal amount, the defect is egregious (fāḥish) and termination is permitted. This is the key threshold.
'Fāḥish' is defined technically, not left to general impression.
4
Apply the fāḥish threshold to a scenario
Consider a mill that grinds only 40% of normal capacity. Since 40% is less than half, the defect is egregious; the lessee may terminate. If it grinds 60%, termination is not allowed, but rent reduction may be sought.
The threshold is quantitative: below 50% qualifies as fāḥish.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب فسخ الإجارة. انكسار ذلك، وكذا ليس للمستأجر أن يمنع منه. وفي النوادر: بنى المؤجر الدار كلها قبل الفسخ فللمستأجر أن يفسخ العقد إن شاء وهو مخالف لما تقدم. ولو انقطع ماء الرحى والبيت وبقي ما ينتفع به لغير الطحن فعليه من الأجر بحصته لأنه بقي شيء من المعقود عليه إذا استوفاه لزمه حصته. وقوله وخراب الدار إلى آخره يفيد أن الإجارة تنفسخ بهذه الأشياء. وفي الذخيرة: الإجارة في الرحى لا تنفسخ بانقطاع وفي الخانية: فإن بني الدار بعد الفسخ فليس للمستأجر أن يسكنها. وفي التتارخانية: والسفينة المستأجرة إذا نقضت وصارت ألواحاً ثم أعيدت سفينة أخرى لم يجز تسليمها للمستأجر. اهـ. ومثل انقطاع ماء الرحى الحجر. وفي التتارخانية: ولو استأجره ليزرع أرضه ببذره ثم بدا له أن لا يزرع كان عذراً، ولو استأجر أرضاً ليزرعها فغرقت أو تربت أو سبخت كان ذلك عذراً في فسخها. وفي الأصل: استأجر أرضاً ليزرعها شيئاً سماه فزرعها ذلك وأصاب الزرع آفة وذهب وفت الزراعة لذلك الزرع فأراد أن يزرع ما هو أقل منه ضرراً أو مثله فله ذلك وإلا فسخت ولزمه ما مضى من الأجرة قيد بانقطاع الرحى ليحترز عن النقصان في الرحا، فإن كان النقصان فاحشاً فله حق الفسخ، وإن كان غير فاحش فليس له حق الفسخ. قال القدوري: إذا صار الطحن أقل من نصف الحنطة أو لا فهو فاحش.
Chapter of Ijarah: Section of Terminating Ijarah. Breaking that, and likewise it is not for the lessee to prevent him from it. And in al-Nawadir: If the lessor built the entire house before the termination, the lessee has the option to terminate the contract if he wishes, and it contradicts what preceded. And if the water of the mill and the house stopped, and there remains something beneficial other than grinding, then he owes rent proportionate to it because part of the contracted subject-matter remains; when he receives it, its portion becomes binding. And his statement 'and the ruin of the house, etc.' indicates that the lease is terminated by these things. And in al-Dhakhira: The lease of the mill is not terminated by the stoppage. And in al-Khaniya: If the house was built after the termination, it is not for the lessee to dwell in it. And similar to the stoppage of the mill's water is the stone. And in al-TatarKhaniya: If he hired him to sow his land with his own seed, then he changed his mind not to sow, it is an excuse. And if he hired land to sow it, and it was flooded, or became soiled, or became alkaline, that is an excuse for its termination. And in al-Asl: He hired land to sow it with something he named, and he sowed it with that, and a blight befell the crop and it perished, and the planting season passed for that crop, so he wants to sow something less harmful or similar; he may do so, otherwise the lease is terminated and he owes what has passed of the rent. Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings regarding termination of a lease (ijarah) due to various defects or excuses (a'dhar). The discussion draws from multiple Hanafi sources: al-Nawadir, al-Dhakhira, al-Khaniya, and al-TatarKhaniya. The first scenario deals with the lessor building upon the leased property before termination; if he builds the entire house, the lessee may terminate. If the water supply for a mill or house is cut off, but some benefit remains (e.g., use of the building for other purposes), the lessee must pay rent proportionate to that benefit. If the mill's water stops, the lease does not automatically terminate according to al-Dhakhira. If the lessor rebuilds after termination, the lessee cannot re-enter. If a ship is dismantled and rebuilt into a different vessel, it cannot be delivered to the lessee. Similar rulings apply to land leases: if the land is damaged by flooding or salinization, it is an excuse for termination. If the lessee sows something and the crop is destroyed, he may sow a less harmful alternative or terminate, paying rent for the period used. The author quotes al-Quduri's definition of egregious deficiency: when grinding capacity drops below half of normal.

Key Terms
عذر ('udhr): A valid excuse that permits termination of a lease, such as stoppage of water, destruction of property, or inability to use the leased object as intended.
فاحش (fāhish): Egregious; a deficiency that exceeds half of the normal utility, e.g., grinding less than half of the usual amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When grinding stops completely
B) When grinding becomes less than half of the normal amount

D) When the water supply is interrupted for one day

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a lease may be terminated only if the defect is egregious (fahish), defined as a reduction to less than half of normal utility.

Termination of Lease by Death of a Party (For Self)
Ruling that a lease terminates upon the death of either party, with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lease termination upon death, explain the rational proof (dalil aqli), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A lease terminates upon death because benefits are consumed moment by moment.

In this passage, we encounter a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a lease contract survive the death of either party? The Hanafi school holds that it automatically terminates, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues it continues like a sale. The disagreement turns on the nature of a lease: is it a single obligation or a series of incremental transfers of benefit? Let us examine the Hanafi proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The lease terminates automatically upon the death of either party when the contract is for oneself. No judge's ruling is necessary, though some Hanafis require one.
The preferred (mufta bihi) view is automatic termination.
2
Identify the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that death does not invalidate the lease; the contract continues for the benefit of the heirs.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof (dalil aqli)
The lease contract is renewed moment by moment as benefits accrue. The lessor's death ends his ownership of future benefits, so the contract terminates.
The key Arabic phrase: 'al-'aqd yan'aqid sa'atan fa sa'atan hasba huduth al-manfa'ah'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the desert objection
The objector cites the case where a hired animal's owner dies mid-journey and the Hirer may continue. The Hanafi answer is necessity: if no alternative exists, the contract continues to avoid harm.
If an alternative animal or judge is available, the objection stands and the lease terminates.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the Hanafi school, the heirs cannot demand the remaining rent; in the Shafi'i school, they can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وتفسخ بموت أحد عقدها لنفسه) قال الشارح: وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يحتاج إلى حكم الحاكم ا هـ. والظاهر أن فيه إشارة إليه قال في المفيد والمزيد وقال بعضهم لا لكن يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ويقضي بالفسخ ولا يحتاج في ذلك إلى دعوى وللعلماء في ذلك طريقان: أحدهما أن يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي بالفسخ. الثانية أن يبيع العين المؤجرة ويحكم القاضي فيها بالصحة وانفساخ الأولى وهي طريقة ما وراء النهر. وقال الشافعي: لا تبطل بموت أحدهما. ولنا أن العقد ينعقد ساعة فساعة حسب حدوث المنفعة فإذا مات المؤجر انتقل الملك إلى الوارث ومنفعته إليه والمنافع المستحقة بالعقد هي المملوكة للمؤجر وقد فات بموته فتنفسخ. قال في العتابية: ونوقض بما إذا استأجر دابة إلى مكان معين فمات صاحب الدابة وسط الطريق كان للمستأجر أن يركبها إلى المكان المسمى وقد مات أحدهما أو عقدها لنفسه. وأجبت بأن ذلك للضرورة وأنه يخاف على نفسه وماله حيث لا يجدد دابة أخرى في وسط المفازة ولا يكون ثمة قاض يرفع الأمر إليه حتى قال بعض مشايخنا: إن وجد ثمة دابة أخرى يحمل عليها متاعه ينتقض أو وجد قاض ينتقض ا.هـ. وفي المحيط: إذا مات رب الدابة نظر القاضي ما هو الأصلح للورثة؛ إن رأى بيع الجمل وحفظ الثمن أنفع للورثة، فعل، وإن رأى إبقاء الإجارة فإن كان بقية فالأفضل الإبقاء، وإن كان غير بقية والأفضل فسخها، فإن فسخها وأقام البينة أنه أوفاه الكراء رد عليه بحساب ما بقي ولو أنفق المستأجر على الدابة شيئاً لم يحسب له إلا  كتاب الإجارة باب فسخ الإجارة وتفسخ بخيار الشرط وبخيار الرؤية وتفسخ بالعذر وهو عجز أحد العاقدين عن المضي إذا كان بإذن القاضي .اهـ. وفيه أيضاً وإذا مات أحدهما وفي الأرض زرع يترك إلى الحصاد ويكون على المستأجر أو على ورثته ما بقي من الأجر لأنها كما تفسخ بالأعذار تبقى بالأعذار ا هـ. وأطلق في الموت فشمل الموت الحكمي كالارتداد وكذا في المحيط. وفي الذخيرة: وإذا سكن بعد الانفساخ بغير عقد فالأصح إن كانت معدة للاشتغال تلزمه أجرة المثل وإلا فلا لأنه غاصب.
He (May Allah have mercy on him) said: (And it terminates by the death of one of the parties when the contract is for himself.) The commentator said: In it is an indication that it does not require a judge's ruling. And it is apparent that there is an indication to it. It is said in al-Mufeed and al-Mazeed: And some said no, but one raises the matter to the judge and he rules for termination, and there is no need for litigation. Scholars have two methods regarding this: one is to raise the matter to the judge for termination. The second is that the judge sells the leased property and rules for its validity and the termination of the first lease; this is the method of Transoxiana. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not invalidated by the death of one of them. Our proof: The contract is concluded moment by moment according to the occurrence of the benefit. So when the lessor dies, ownership transfers to the heir, and the benefit goes to him. The benefits due under the contract are the property of the lessor and have perished by his death, so the contract terminates. It is said in al-Atabiyya: It was objected by the case of hiring an animal to a specific place; when the owner of the animal dies mid-road, the lessee may ride it to the named place even though one of them died, and the contract was for himself. The answer: That is due to necessity, and he fears for himself and his property where he cannot find another animal in the middle of the desert and there is no judge to raise the matter, until some of our teachers said: If he finds another animal there to carry his goods, the objection stands; or if he finds a judge, it stands. End. And in al-Muhit: When the owner of the animal dies, the judge looks at what is best for the heirs: if he sees selling the camel and preserving the price is more beneficial for the heirs, he does so; if he sees maintaining the lease, if it is beneficial, maintaining is better; if it is not beneficial and termination is better, he terminates it. If he terminates and the lessee proves that he paid the rent, the judge returns to him the proportion remaining. And if the lessee spent something on the animal, it is not accounted for except... [PAGE_064] Book of Ijarah, Section of Terminating Ijarah. And it is terminated by the option of stipulation, by the option of inspection, and it is terminated by an excuse, which is the inability of one of the two contractors to proceed, if by permission of the judge. End. And in it also: When one of them dies and there is a crop in the land, it is left until harvest, and the lessee or his heirs owe the remaining rent because, just as it is terminated by excuses, it remains by excuses. End. And he generalized death to include legal death like apostasy, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Dhakhira: If he resides after termination without a contract, the correct view is that if it was prepared for work, he owes the equivalent rent; otherwise, no, because he is a usurper.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage deals with the termination of a lease by the death of either party when the contract is made for oneself. The author first states the ruling that death terminates such a lease, and the commentator adds that no judge's ruling is necessary for the termination, though some scholars require raising the matter to a judge. Two methods are mentioned: the judge may simply pronounce termination, or he may sell the leased property and declare the original lease void, which is the Transoxiana method. Then the passage presents the Shafi'i objection: al-Shafi'i holds that death does not invalidate the lease. The Hanafi proof is rational (dalil aqli): the lease contract is renewed moment by moment as benefits accrue. When the lessor dies, ownership of the benefits transfers to the heir, and the benefits that were due under the contract have perished with the lessor's death, so the contract terminates. An objection is raised: if someone hires a riding animal to a specific place and the owner dies mid-trip, the Hanafis allow the lessee to continue to the destination. How does that square with the rule? The answer is necessity: in the desert, with no alternative animal or judge, the lessee is permitted to continue out of necessity. If an alternative exists, the objection stands. The passage also discusses the judge's role in deciding the best course for the heirs after the lessor's death. It then mentions that if a crop is in the ground at the time of death, the lease continues until harvest. Finally, it states that if someone resides in the property after termination without a new contract, he must pay the equivalent rent if it was a commercial property, because he is a usurper.

Key Terms
موت حكمي (mawt hukmī): Legal death, such as apostasy (ridda), which is treated like actual death for the purposes of terminating a lease.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market rental value; paid by a usurper who uses property without a valid contract after termination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof that a lease terminates upon the death of the lessor?
A) Quranic verse on inheritance
B) Hadith that contracts end with death
C) The contract is renewed moment by moment; the lessor's death ends his ownership of future benefits
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
A lease contract terminates upon death of either party because it is formed moment by moment; the lessor's death ends his capacity to deliver future benefits.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Termination of Lease by Death and by Option of Stipulation
Rulings on lease termination by death in representation and by option stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on termination of lease when the contract is for another (agent/trustee) and EXPLAIN the validity of stipulating an option to terminate in ijarah using qiyas, including the Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
A lease made by an agent does not void on the agent's death; stipulating an option to terminate in lease is valid by analogy to sale.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two specific scenarios of lease termination: first, when the contract is made by a representative (agent, executor, trustee) and one party dies; second, when either party stipulates an option to rescind the lease. Both cases involve fundamental Hanafi principles of contractual analogy and the permissibility of options in exchange contracts. The Shafi'i school opposes the latter, leading to a clear inter-madhhab dispute resolved by the Hanafi qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish termination by death: agent vs. principal
Read the first ruling: if the agent (wakil, wasi, mutawalli) who contracted dies, the lease does not void because the entitlement belongs to the principal. But if the principal for whom the contract was made dies, the lease becomes void. Note the difference.
The author generalizes 'agent' to include both leasing out and hiring.
2
Analyze the joint lessee/lessor case and Zufar's objection
When one co-lessee or co-lessor dies, the lease voids only in the deceased's share, not the whole, according to the majority. Zufar argues the entire lease voids due to joint ownership preventing continuation. The Hanafi response: tolerance in continuation differs from initial formation.
This illustrates the principle of tasamuh (tolerance) in ongoing contracts.
3
Understand the agent-for-hiring scenario and delivery issue
From al-Dhakhira: if an agent hired a property but died before delivery, the lease voids; if delivery occurred, it remains valid. Also note the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad when the agent refuses to hand over the property.
This shows the importance of possession in agency contracts.
4
Examine the khiyar al-shart dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
The Hanafi school allows stipulating an option to terminate for up to three days in ijarah. Al-Shafi'i rejects it because the subject (benefits) cannot be fully returned. Identify the core issue and both arguments.
The dispute hinges on whether ijarah is analogous to sale for options.
5
Follow the Hanafi qiyas proof and address exceptions
The Hanafi proof: ijarah is an exchange contract, admits iqala, and does not require immediate delivery; therefore, khiyar is valid by qiyas on sale. Exceptions: nikah (not exchange), sarf and salam (due to specific impediments).
This qiyas is jali (clear) because both contracts share the same illa of deliberation need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن عقدها لغيره لا كالوكيل والوصي والمتولي في الوقف) يعني تفسخ بموت أحدهما إذا كان عقدها لغيره كما ذكرنا لبقاء المستحق عليه، والمستحق لو مات المعقود له بطلت لما ذكرنا وإذا مات أحد المستأجرين أو المؤجرين بطلت الإجارة في نصيبه وبقيت في نصيب الحي. وقال زفر: بطلت في نصيب الحي أيضاً لأن الشيوع مانع من الإجارة. قلنا ذلك في الابتداء لا في البقاء لأنه يتسامح في البقاء ما لا يتسامح في الابتداء. وأطلق في الوكيل فشمل الوكيل بالإيجار والوكيل بالاستئجار. قال في الذخيرة: وأما الوكيل بالاستئجار إذا مات تبطل الإجارة لأن التوكيل بالاستئجار توكيل شراء المنافع فيصير مشترياً لنفسه ثم يصير مؤجراً من الموكل. اهـ. أقول: لعل هذا إذا لم يسلم إلى الموكل، أما لو سلم لا تبطل فتدبره. وفي الظهيرية: أمر رجلاً أن يستأجر داراً بعينها سنة للموكل فاستأجرها المأمور وتسلمها وأبى أن يدفعها للآمر حتى مضت السنة قال أبو يوسف: أجر عليه ولا على الآمر. وقال محمد: يجب الأجر على الآمر. ولم يتعرض لما إذا قبض الناظر الأجرة معجلة أو غيره ثم مات فنقول: إذا كان الوقف أهلياً والغلة للقابض فآجر وقبض الأجرة معجلة ثم مات قبل انتهاء المدة ففي الفتاوى وغيرها للذي انتقل له الحق أن يأخذ من المستأجر أجرة ما آل إليه بالموت، فإن كان الميت ترك مالاً رجع بذلك على ماله، وإن لم يترك مالاً لا. المستأجر يرجع بشيء وضاع عليه، وإن كان الناظر في وقف غير أهلي فمات بعد القبض قبل انتهاء المدة لا يضع ذلك عليه ويرجع على جهة الوقف وفي مال الميت المتروك. قال رحمه الله: (وتفسخ بخيار الشرط) يعني إذا شرط المؤجر أو المستأجر خيار الشرط أو شرط كل منهما خيار الشرط ثلاثة أيام فله أن يفسخ الإجارة به عندنا. وقال الإمام الشافعي: لا يصح شرط الخيار في الإجارة لأن المستأجر لا يمكنه رد المعقود عليه بكماله إن كان الخيار له، وإن كان المشروط له الخيار المؤجر لا يمكنه التسليم أيضاً على الكمال لأن المنافع تحدث ساعة فساعة. ولنا أنه عقد معاوضة ولا يجب قبضه في المجلس، ويحتمل الفسخ بالإقالة فيجوز شرط الخيار فيه كالبيع ولأن الخيار شرط في البيع للتروي فكذا في الإجارة لأنها تقع بغتة من غير سابقة تأمل. فيمكن أن يقع غير موافق فيحتاج إلى الإقالة فيجوز اشتراط الخيار فيها بخلاف النكاح لأنه ليس بمعاوضة فلا يصح شرط الخيار فيه، وبخلاف الصرف والسلم فلا يصح شرط.
He (May Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he made the contract for another, like the agent, executor, and trustee of the endowment) meaning it terminates by the death of one of them when the contract is for another, as we mentioned, because the entitlement remains with the principal. If the one for whom the contract was made dies, it becomes void as we mentioned. And if one of the co-lessees or co-lessors dies, the lease becomes void in his share and remains in the share of the living. Zufar said: It becomes void in the share of the living also because joint ownership prevents the lease. We said: That applies initially, not in continuation, because in continuation tolerances are allowed that are not allowed initially. And he generalized the agent to include the agent for leasing out and the agent for hiring. It is said in al-Dhakhira: As for the agent for hiring, if he dies, the lease becomes void because the agency for hiring is an agency to purchase benefits; thus he becomes a purchaser for himself and then becomes a lessor for the principal. End. I say: Perhaps this is if he did not deliver to the principal; if he delivered, it does not become void, so consider it. And in al-Zahiriya: A man ordered another to hire a specific house for a year for the principal. The agent hired it and took possession, but refused to hand it over to the principal until the year ended. Abu Yusuf said: The rent is owed by the agent, not the principal. Muhammad said: The rent is owed by the principal. And he did not address the case where the trustee (nazir) received the rent in advance or otherwise then died. So we say: If the endowment is private (ahli) and the revenue is for the receiver, and he leased and received the rent in advance, then died before the end of the term – according to the fatawa and others, the one to whom the right transfers may take from the lessee the rent for the period up to the death. If the deceased left property, he recovers from his estate; if he left no property, no. The lessee does not recover anything; it is lost on him. And if the trustee of a non-private endowment (ghayr ahli) dies after receipt before the end of the term, it is not lost on him; he recovers from the endowment and the deceased's estate. He (May Allah have mercy on him) said: (And it is terminated by the option of stipulation) meaning if the lessor or lessee stipulates an option of stipulation, or each of them stipulates an option of stipulation for three days, then he may terminate the lease thereby according to us. Imam al-Shafi'i said: The stipulation of an option is not valid in a lease because if the option is for the lessee, he cannot return the entire leased item; if it is for the lessor, he cannot deliver it completely either because benefits arise moment by moment. Our proof: It is a contract of exchange, and delivery in the session is not required; it admits of termination by mutual agreement (iqala), so stipulating an option is permissible, like in sale. And because the option is stipulated in sale for deliberation, so too in lease, because it occurs abruptly without prior contemplation. It may turn out unsuitable, so needing iqala, therefore stipulating an option is permissible. Unlike marriage, which is not an exchange, so stipulating an option is not valid. And unlike currency exchange (sarf) and salam, where stipulation is not valid.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but related topics: termination by death when the lease is made by an agent or representative for another person, and the validity of stipulating an option to terminate in a lease contract. First, the author states that if the contract is made by an agent (like a representative or trustee), the rule differs: if the agent dies, the lease does not automatically terminate because the entitlement belongs to the principal. However, if the principal (the one for whom the contract was made) dies, the lease becomes void. The passage then discusses the case of joint lessees or lessors: if one dies, the lease is void only in his share, not the whole, contrary to Zufar's view that joint ownership invalidates the entire lease. The author then examines the case of an agent for hiring: according to al-Dhakhira, if the agent dies before delivering the property to the principal, the lease becomes void; but if he had already delivered, it remains valid. A specific scenario from al-Zahiriya is presented: an agent hires a house but refuses to hand it over; Abu Yusuf holds the agent liable for rent, while Muhammad holds the principal liable. The passage also discusses the death of a waqf trustee who collected rent in advance, detailing the recovery of rent from the lessee and the deceased's estate depending on whether the waqf is 'ahli' (private) or 'ghayr ahli' (public). The second major topic is the validity of stipulating an option to terminate (khiyar al-shart) in a lease. According to the Hanafis, such a stipulation (usually for three days) is valid. This is based on analogy with sale (qiyas jaliy): both are contracts of exchange, and an option can be stipulated for deliberation. The Hanafi proof also relies on the fact that a lease can be terminated by mutual agreement (iqala), so an option is even more appropriate. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the subject matter (benefits) cannot be returned completely. The Hanafi response is that the option is valid because the lease is an exchange contract that does not require immediate delivery of the entire benefit. The passage notes exceptions: nikah (marriage) is not an exchange, so no option; and sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance purchase) do not permit option stipulation.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): The right to terminate a contract within a stipulated period (usually three days) if one party stipulates it at the time of contracting.
وكيل بالاستئجار (wakīl bi-al-isti'jār): An agent hired to lease (take on rent) a property on behalf of another.
وقف أهلي (waqf ahlī): A private waqf (family endowment) where the revenue is for a specific beneficiary (the 'qabid').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) valid in a lease contract?
A) Because the Prophet (PBUH) explicitly permitted it
B) Because it is an exchange contract, and termination by mutual agreement (iqala) is possible, so an option is valid by analogy to sale
C) Because the lease is not binding until the term begins
D) Because the lessor and lessee can agree on any condition

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a lease made by an agent does not void upon the agent's death, and stipulating a three-day option to cancel is valid by qiyas on sale.

Death of a Joint Lessee: Partial vs Total Termination of Ijarah
Explaining consequences of death and agency in Ijarah termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that death of a joint lessee voids only his share and evaluate Zufar's opposing argument using the inception-continuation distinction.

Core Idea
Death of a joint lessee voids only his share; the lease continues for the living lessee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a key ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: does the death of one joint lessee void the entire lease or only his portion? The answer reveals a deeper principle about tolerance in the continuation of contracts versus their inception. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi legal reasoning to tenancy issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three general causes of ijarah termination
The author lists khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, and 'udhr (excuse). Death is an 'udhr that triggers termination.
The text also mentions the crop example, which shows that the contract may be preserved by excuse.
2
State the rule for joint lessees' death
When one of multiple lessees dies, the lease becomes void only in his share and continues in the shares of the living lessees.
This applies equally to joint lessors.
3
Analyze Zufar's opposing view
Zufar argues that the entire lease becomes void because co-ownership (shuyu') prevents the validity of ijarah at inception, so it should also prevent continuation.
Zufar is a leading Hanafi scholar, so this is an intra-madhhab dispute.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response using the ibtida'-baqa' distinction
The rebuttal: what is forbidden at inception (ibtida') may be tolerated in continuation (baqa'). This is a standard Hanafi usul principle allowing flexibility in ongoing contracts.
The Arabic phrase: 'يتسامح في البقاء ما لا يتسامح في الابتداء'.
5
Extend the rule to agency and waqf cases
If an agent dies before delivering the leased property, the lease is void. If delivered, it remains valid. For a trustee receiving advance rent then dying, the ruling differs based on waqf type.
This shows the principle applies across different scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب فسخ الإجارة
وتفسخ بخيار الشرط وبخيار الرؤية وتفسخ بالعذر وهو عجز أحد العاقدين عن المضي إذا كان بإذن القاضي .اهـ. وفيه أيضاً وإذا مات أحدهما وفي الأرض زرع يترك إلى الحصاد ويكون على المستأجر أو على ورثته ما بقي من الأجر لأنها كما تفسخ بالأعذار تبقى بالأعذار ا هـ. وأطلق في الموت فشمل الموت الحكمي كالارتداد وكذا في المحيط. وفي الذخيرة: وإذا سكن بعد الانفساخ بغير عقد فالأصح إن كانت معدة للاشتغال تلزمه أجرة المثل وإلا فلا لأنه غاصب .
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن عقدها لغيره لا كالوكيل والوصي والمتولي في الوقف) يعني تفسخ بموت أحدهما إذا كان عقدها لغيره كما ذكرنا لبقاء المستحق عليه، والمستحق لو مات المعقود له بطلت لما ذكرنا وإذا مات أحد المستأجرين أو المؤجرين بطلت الإجارة في نصيبه وبقيت في نصيب الحي. وقال زفر : بطلت في نصيب الحي أيضاً لأن الشيوع مانع من الإجارة. قلنا ذلك في الابتداء لا في البقاء لأنه يتسامح في البقاء ما لا يتسامح في الابتداء . وأطلق في الوكيل فشمل الوكيل بالإيجار والوكيل بالاستئجار. قال في الذخيرة: وأما الوكيل بالاستئجار إذا مات تبطل الإجارة لأن التوكيل بالاستئجار توكيل شراء المنافع فيصير مشترياً لنفسه ثم يصير مؤجراً من الموكل .اهـ. أقول : لعل هذا إذا لم يسلم إلى الموكل، أما لو سلم لا تبطل فتدبره. وفي الظهيرية : أمر رجلاً أن يستأجر داراً بعينها سنة للموكل فاستأجرها المأمور وتسلمها وأبى أن يدفعها للآمر حتى مضت السنة قال أبو يوسف : أجر عليه ولا على الآمر . وقال محمد : يجب الأجر على الآمر . ولم يتعرض لما إذا قبض الناظر الأجرة معجلة أو غيره ثم مات فنقول : إذا كان الوقف أهلياً والغلة للقابض فآجر وقبض الأجرة معجلة ثم مات قبل انتهاء المدة ففي الفتاوى وغيرها للذي انتقل له الحق أن يأخذ من المستأجر أجرة ما آل إليه بالموت، فإن كان الميت ترك مالاً رجع بذلك على ماله، وإن لم يترك مالاً لا . المستأجر يرجع بشيء وضاع عليه، وإن كان الناظر في وقف غير أهلي فمات بعد القبض قبل انتهاء المدة لا يضع ذلك عليه ويرجع على جهة الوقف وفي مال الميت المتروك.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter of Termination of Ijarah. And it is terminated by option of stipulation, option of inspection, and by excuse which is inability of either contracting party to proceed if [the termination] is by permission of the judge. End. And in it also: If one of them dies and there is a crop in the land, it is left until harvest, and the remaining rent is due from the lessee or his heirs because, just as [the contract] is terminated by excuses, it remains [in effect] by excuses. End. And he [the author] made death absolute, so it includes legal death like apostasy, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Dhakhira: If he resides after termination without a contract, the correct view is that if [the property] was prepared for occupation, he is liable for the market rent; otherwise not, because he is a usurper. He (Abu Hanifa) said: (And if he contracted for another, such as the agent, executor, and trustee of a waqf) meaning that [the contract] is terminated by the death of one of them if he contracted for another as we mentioned, due to the continuance of the claim upon him, and if the person for whom the contract was made dies, it is invalidated as we mentioned. If one of the joint lessees or lessors dies, the lease is void in his share and remains in the share of the living. Zufar said: It is void in the living's share as well, because co-ownership prevents lease. We said: That is at the beginning, not in continuance, because what is tolerated in continuance is not tolerated at the beginning. And he [the author] made the agent absolute, so it includes the agent for leasing and the agent for hiring. In al-Dhakhira: As for the agent for hiring, if he dies, the lease is void because authorization for hiring is authorization to purchase benefits, so he becomes a buyer for himself, then becomes a lessor for the principal. End. I say: This is perhaps if he has not delivered [the property] to the principal; if he has delivered, it does not become void, so reflect. In al-Dhahiriyya: A man ordered another to hire a specific house for a year for the principal, so the agent hired and took possession and refused to give it to the principal until the year passed. Abu Yusuf said: The rent is against the agent, not the principal. Muhammad said: The rent is due from the principal. And he did not address the case where the trustee received the rent in advance or otherwise and then died. So we say: If the waqf is private and the produce is for the receiver, then he leased and received the rent in advance and then died before the end of the term, according to the fatawa etc., the one to whom the right passes may take from the lessee the rent for what has passed due to death. If the deceased left property, he can claim it from his estate; if he left no property, he cannot. The lessee does not get anything back and loses it. If the trustee of a non-private waqf dies after receipt before the end of the term, it is not lost on him [the trustee?] and he can claim from the waqf entity and from the deceased's estate.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage, from the beginning of the chapter on termination of ijarah in al-Bahr al-Raiq, first states the general causes of termination: khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection), and 'udhr (excuse), the last being the inability of either party to proceed, subject to the judge's permission. Then it gives a detailed example: if the lessee dies while there is a crop on the land, the contract remains in effect until harvest, and the remaining rent is payable. Death is interpreted broadly, including legal death such as apostasy. If the lessee remains in possession after termination without a new contract, he is liable for market rent only if the property was for commercial activity; otherwise, he is a usurper. The text then discusses contracts made by agents, executors, or trustees. If the contract was made on behalf of another, the death of the contracting party (agent) terminates the lease because the principal remains entitled. But if the principal dies, it becomes void. In joint leases, if one lessee dies, the lease is void only in his share; the living share continues. Zufar disagreed, arguing that co-ownership prevents the contract's continuance, but the Hanafi position is that what is tolerated in continuation is not tolerated at inception. For a hiring agent, his death voids the contract because he becomes a buyer for himself and then a lessor. These rulings are based on the principle that the contract can be terminated by excuses (like death) and also can be preserved by excuses (like the crop). The passage concludes with practical cases about advance payment of rent by a trustee who dies before the term ends, distinguishing between private and non-private waqf.

Key Terms
فسخ الإجارة (faskh al-ijarah): Termination of a lease contract, which can occur by option, inspection, or excuse.
عذر (udhr): An excuse that prevents the party from fulfilling the contract, e.g., death, inability to proceed without excessive harm.
شيوع (shuyu'): Co-ownership or undivided shares in a property or contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if one of two joint lessees dies, what happens to the ijarah?
A) The entire lease becomes void.
B) The lease remains valid for both shares.
C) The lease is void only in the deceased's share and remains in the living's share.
D) The lease is automatically renewed for the living lessee.

Key Takeaway
Death of a joint lessee voids only his share, based on the principle that tolerance in continuation is greater than in inception.
