كتاب المزارعة
فالخارج على الشرط فإن لم يخرج شيء فلا شيء للعامل ومن أبى عن المضي أجبر إلا للتبن صحت لأنه هو المقصود والتبن نصفان ولو شرطا الحب نصفين والتين لرب الأرض صحت لأنه شرط لا يخالفه العقد لأنه نماء ملكه ولو شرطا التبن للعامل فسد فلأنه شرط مخالف لمقتضى العقد فربما يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة بأن يصيب الزرع آفة فلا ينعقد الحب ولا يخرج إلا التبن قال : والعشر عليهما عندهما، وعند الإمام على صاحب الأرض، فإن لم يأخذ الإمام العشر فهو لصاحب الأرض عند الإمام وعندهما لهما ولو قال صاحب الأرض للعامل لا أدري ما يأخذ الإمام العشر أو النصف لأن النصف لي بعدما يأخذ جازت عندهما؛ كذا في المحيط قال رحمه الله : ( فإن صحت فالخارج على الشرط لصحة الالتزام. قال في المحيط : وأما الزيادة والحط في المزارعة والمعاملة فالأفضل إن كان المعقود عليه بحال يجوز ابتداء المزارعة والمعاملة جازت الزيادة فيهما، وإذا أدى أحدهما الآخر في الخارج فإن كان حال الزيادة قبل الاستحصاد وعظم التناهي تجوز الزيادة لأنه يجوز ابتداء العقد ما دام قابلاً للزيادة وإلا فلا، والحط جائز في الحالين حال قبول الزيادة وبعدها لأنه إسقاط. ولو باع الأرض المدفوعة مزارعة أو معاملة فالبيع موقف على إجازة المزارع والعامل، فإن يجز تبقى إلى انتهاء المزارعة والمعاملة ويخير المشتري إن شاء انتظر أو فسخ ولم يتعرض المؤلف لما إذا وقع في العقد أو علق ونحن نبين ذلك قال وفيه أيضاً : لو دفع الأرض والبذر سنة على أن يزرعها بغير كراب فللعامل ربع الخارج وإن كربها فثلثه وإن كرب وبنى فنصفه جاز ما شرطاه، وكذا لو كان البذر من جهة المزارع القسم الثاني دفع الأرض على أن يزرعها حنطة فالخارج كذا، وإن زرعها شعيراً فكذا وإن زرعها سمسماً فكذا فهذا على أربعة أوجه : أما إن قال ازرعها أو زرعت فيها أو زرعت منها أو زرعت بعضاً منها فالمزارعة في الأولين جائزة لأنه خيره بين العقود الثلاثة، فإن زرع شيئاً من الأصناف الثلاثة فالخارج على ما شرطاه، ولو قال ما زرعت منها أو بعضاً منها فالمزارعة فاسدة لأنه إن زرع البعض حنطة والبعض شعيراً وسمسماً فذلك البعض مجهول، ولو كان البذر من قبل العامل وشرط إن زرعها حنطة فبينهما نصفان وإن زرعها شعيراً فذلك للعامل جاز استحساناً وهو في الأول مزارعة وفي الثاني إعارة الأرض . ثم ذكر محمد التخيير بين ثلاثة ولم يذكر هل يجوز التخيير في أكثر من ذلك؟ روى هشام أنه لا يجوز القسم الثالث دفع الأرض على أن زرعها ببذره في أول جمادى الاولى فالخارج نصفان وإن أخر فالثلث للمزارع فالشرطان جائزان عندهما وبيان الدليل يطلب فيه اهـ .
قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يخرج شيء فلا شيء للعامل لأنها إما اجاره أو شركة، فإن كانت اجارة فالواجب في العقد الصحيح منها المسمى وهو معدوم فلا يستحق غيره، وإن كانت شركة فالشركة في الخارج دون غيره فلا يستحق غيره بخلاف ما إذا فسدت المزارعة ولم رب البذر وتبطل بموت أحدهما فإن مضت المدة والزرع لم يدرك فعلى الزارع أجر مثل تخرج الأرض حيث يستحق أجر المثل في المدة وعدم الخروج لا يمنع وجوبه. قال في العناية : واستشكل بمن استأجر أرضاً بعين ففعل الأجير وهلكت العين قبل التسليم فإنه على المستأجر أجرة المثل فليكن هذا مثله لأن المزارعة قد صحت والأجر مسمى وهلك الأجر . وأجيب بأن الأجر ههنا هلك بعد التسليم لأن المزارع قبض البذر الذي يتفرع منه الخارج وقبض الأصل قبض لفروعه والآخر المعين إلى الأجر لا يجب للآخر شيء فكذا هنا. ولقائل أن يقول : هذا الجواب غير مستقيم في صورة استئجار الأرض فإن رب الأرض لا يقبض البذر الذي يتفرع منه الخارج حتى يكون قبضه قبضاً لفرغه قال رحمه الله : (ومن أبى عن المضي أجبر إلا رب البذر لأنها انعقدت اجارة والأجارة عقد لازم غير إنها تنفسخ بالعذر، فإن امتنع صاحب البذر عن المضي فيها كان معذوراً لأنه لا يمكنه المضي إلا باتلاف ماله وهو إلقاء البذر على الأرض ولا يدري هل يخرج أم لا فصار نظير ما لو استأجره لهدم داره ثم امتنع، وإن امتنع العامل أجبر على العمل، وإن امتنع رب البذر والأرض من قبله بعدما كرب الأرض فلا شيء له في عمل الكراب في القضاء لأن عمله إنما يتقوم بالعقد وقد فوته بجزء من الخارج فلا خارج ويلزمه فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى أجر مثله له كيلاً يكون مغروراً من جهته لأنه يتضرر به وهو مدفوع فيكتفي بإرضائه بأن يوفيه أجر مثله. قال رحمه الله : وتبطل بموت أحدهما لأنها إجارة وهي تبطل بموت أحد المتعاقدين إذا عقدها لنفسه وقد بيناه في الاجارة، وهذا الاطلاق جواب القياس وفي الاستحسان إذا مات وقد نبت الزرع يبقى عقد الاجارة حتى يحصد الزرع ثم يبطل في الباقي لأن في ابقائه هذه المدة مراعاة الحقين فيعمل العامل أو وارثه على حالة، فإذا حصد يقسم على ما شرطاه ولا ضرورة في الباقي. ولو مات رب الأرض قبل الزرع بعدما كرب الأرض وحفر الأنهار انتقضت المزارعة لأنه ليس في ذلك إتلاف مال على الزارع ولا شيء للعامل بمقابلة العمل لأنه يقوم بالخارج ولا خارج، ولا يجب شيء بخلاف المسئلة الأولى حيث يقضي بإرضائه لأنه مغرور من جهته باختياره، وإذا كان على رب الأرض دين ولم يقدر على قضائه إلا ببيع الأرض فسخت المزارعة قبل الزرع وبيعت بالدين ولا شيء للعامل عليه في الكرب وحفر الأنهار. ولو نبت الزرع ولم يحصد لم بيع الأرض بالدين حتى يستحصد الزرع لأن في البيع إبطال حق المزارع والتأخير أهون من الإبطال ويخرجه القاضي من الحبس إن كان حبسه به لأنه لم يمنع بيع الأرض لم يكن مماطلاً والحبس جزاء المماطلة وفي الذخيرة ولو مات رب الأرض بعد الزرع قبل النبات هل تبقى المزارعة ؟ قال بعضهم تبقى. وقال بعضهم لا تبقى فتفسخ . وفيها أيضاً: وهل يحتاج في فسخ المزارعة إلى قضاء القاضي؟ قيل : وفي رواية الزيادات يحتاج إل القضاء والرضا، وفي رواية كتاب المزارعة لا يحتاج إلى القضاء أو الرضا اهـ. ولو مات
Book of Muzara'ah. So the produce is according to the condition, and if nothing comes out then nothing for the worker. And whoever refuses to proceed is compelled except for the straw? It is valid because it is the intended purpose, and the straw is half each. And if they stipulate the grain half and the figs for the owner of the land, it is valid because it is a condition that does not contradict the contract because it is the growth of his property. And if they stipulate the straw for the worker, it is corrupt because it is a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract, and maybe it leads to cutting the partnership by a blight afflicting the crop so the grain does not form and only straw comes out. He said: And the tithe is upon both according to them, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa upon the owner of the land. If the imam does not take the tithe, then it belongs to the owner of the land according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to them it belongs to both. And if the owner of the land says to the worker: I do not know what the imam will take, the tithe or half, because the half is for me after he takes, it is valid according to them. Likewise in al-Muhit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If it is valid, then the produce is according to the condition due to the validity of the commitment.) He said in al-Muhit: As for increase and decrease in muzara'ah and mu'amalah, the best is if the contracted thing is in a state that allows the initiation of muzara'ah and mu'amalah, then increase in them is permissible. And if one of them gives the other in the produce, if the increase is before harvest and the crop has reached its full growth, increase is permissible because the initiation of the contract is permissible as long as it is capable of increase, otherwise not. And decrease is permissible in both cases, the case of accepting increase and after it, because it is a relinquishment. And if he sells the land given in muzara'ah or mu'amalah, the sale is suspended pending the permission of the muzari' and the worker. If he permits, it remains until the end of the muzara'ah and mu'amalah, and the buyer is given the choice: if he wishes he waits or rescinds. The author did not address when the contract is contingent or conditioned, and we will explain that. He said, and also in it: If he gives the land and seed for a year on condition that he cultivates it without plowing, then for the worker a quarter of the produce; if he plows it, then a third; if he plows and builds, then half; whatever they stipulate is valid. Likewise if the seed is from the muzari'. The second section: giving the land on condition that he cultivates it with wheat, then the produce is such; if he cultivates it with barley, then such; if with sesame, then such. So this is in four aspects: If he says 'cultivate it' or 'you cultivated in it' or 'you cultivated from it' or 'you cultivated some of it', then the muzara'ah in the first two is valid because he gave him a choice between three contracts. If he cultivates something from the three varieties, then the produce is according to what they stipulated. And if he says 'what you cultivated from it' or 'some of it', then the muzara'ah is corrupt because if he cultivates some wheat, some barley, and some sesame, then that part is unknown. And if the seed is from the worker and he stipulates that if he cultivates it with wheat then between them half, and if he cultivates it with barley then that is for the worker, it is valid by istihsan. The first is muzara'ah and the second is loan of land. Then Muhammad mentioned choice among three, but did not mention whether choice is permissible in more than that? Hisham narrated that it is not permissible. Third section: giving the land on condition that he cultivate it with his seed in the first of Jumada al-Ula, then the produce is half, and if he delays then a third for the muzari'. Both conditions are valid according to them, and the explanation of the proof is sought therein. End. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If nothing comes out, then nothing for the worker) because it is either a lease or a partnership. If it is a lease, then the obligatory in a valid contract is the specified [wage], and it is nonexistent so he is not entitled to anything else. If it is a partnership, then the partnership is in the produce only, so he is not entitled to anything else, unlike when the muzara'ah is corrupt and [the seed owner?] and it becomes void by the death of one of them. If the period passes and the crop has not ripened, then the cultivator must pay an equivalent wage for the land where the equivalent wage is due for the period, and the lack of produce does not prevent its obligation. He said in al-Inayah: And it is problematic with one who hires a specific piece of land, then the hired person does the work and the land is destroyed before delivery, then he must pay the equivalent rent. So this should be similar because the muzara'ah was valid and the specified wage was lost. And it was answered that here the wage was lost after delivery because the muzari' took possession of the seed from which the produce branches, and possession of the origin is possession of its branches. And the other specific [wage] is not owed, so here too. And one may say: This answer is not correct in the case of hiring land, because the owner of the land does not take possession of the seed from which the produce branches so that his possession is possession of its branches. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And whoever refuses to proceed is compelled except the owner of the seed) because it is concluded as a lease, and lease is a binding contract, but it is dissolved due to an excuse. If the owner of the seed refuses to proceed, he is excused because he cannot proceed except by destroying his property, which is throwing the seed on the land, and he does not know if it will come out or not, so it becomes similar to if he hired him to demolish his house and then refused. And if the worker refuses, he is compelled to work. And if the owner of the seed and the land refuses after he has plowed the land, then there is nothing for him for the work of plowing in the court because his work is only valued by the contract, and he has forfeited it by [taking] a part of the produce, and there is no produce, and he must in what is between him and Allah the Exalted pay an equivalent wage for it, so that he is not deceived by him. Because he is harmed by it and he is repelled, so he is content by paying him his equivalent wage. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it becomes void by the death of one of them) because it is a lease, and a lease becomes void by the death of one of the contracting parties if he contracted for himself, and we have explained it in the chapter of Ijarah. This absolute statement is the answer of qiyas, and by istihsan, if he dies and the crop has grown, the lease contract remains until the crop is harvested, then it becomes void in the remainder. Because in keeping it for this period is consideration of both rights. So the worker or his heir works accordingly, and when harvested, they divide according to what they stipulated, and there is no need in the remainder. And if the owner of the land dies before planting after plowing and digging canals, the muzara'ah is rescinded because there is no destruction of the worker's property, and nothing for the worker in return for the work because it is valued by the produce and there is no produce. Nothing is owed, unlike the first case where he is compensated because he was deceived by his choice. And if the owner of the land has a debt and cannot pay it except by selling the land, then the muzara'ah is rescinded before planting and the land is sold for the debt, and nothing is owed to the worker for plowing and digging canals. And if the crop has grown but not harvested, the land is not sold for the debt until the crop is harvested because in selling there is nullification of the muzari's right, and delay is easier than nullification. And the judge releases him from prison if he was imprisoned for it because he did not prevent the sale of the land, he was not a dilatory, and imprisonment is the penalty for dilatoriness. And in al-Dhakhirah: If the owner of the land dies after planting but before growth, does the muzara'ah remain? Some said it remains. Some said it does not remain, so it is rescinded. And in it also: Is the rescission of muzara'ah in need of the judge's decree? It was said: And in the narration of al-Ziyadat, it needs the judge's decree and consent, and in the narration of the book of muzara'ah, it does not need the judge's decree or consent. End. And if he dies.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the rulings of muzara'ah (sharecropping) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author, Imam al-Mawsili, presents the matn statements and then expands them with reasoning, citations from other works (al-Muhit, al-Inayah, al-Dhakhirah), and intra-Hanafi discussions. The passage covers three main rulings: (1) distribution of produce and the condition that if nothing comes out, the worker gets nothing; (2) compulsion to proceed with the contract except for the owner of the seed; (3) termination of the contract by death of a party. The commentary uses qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) to derive and refine the rulings. For example, in the first ruling, the author explains that the contract is either a lease (ijara) or a partnership (shirkah), so if no produce comes out, the worker is not entitled to anything because the specified wage (in case of lease) is non-existent, or partnership is only in produce. There is an objection from al-Inayah comparing it to hiring land where the land is destroyed before delivery, but the author defends the ruling by arguing that the wage here is lost after delivery because the seed was taken possession of. In the second ruling, the owner of the seed is excused from being compelled because he cannot proceed without risking his property. The worker is compelled to work. If the owner of both seed and land refuses after plowing, he is not liable in court but must pay an equivalent wage in conscience to avoid deception. The third ruling states that the contract becomes void by death of either party by qiyas, but by istihsan, if the crop has grown, the contract remains until harvest to protect both parties' rights. The passage also includes details about increase and decrease in the contract, different scenarios of specifying crops, and the effect of debt on the land. The overall authority weight is from the commentaries of the later Hanafi scholars (al-Mawsili, etc.), building on the zahir al-riwayah of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
الإجبار (al-ijbār): Compulsion by a judge to enforce contract performance.
العذر (al-ʿudhr): A valid excuse that allows dissolution of a binding contract without penalty.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Equivalent wage, the fair market value for the work performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the owner of both land and seed refuses to proceed after the worker has plowed the land, what is the ruling?
A) The owner is compelled in court to pay an equivalent wage for the plowing.
B) The owner is not liable in court but must pay an equivalent wage in conscience.
C) The worker must forfeit the work without any compensation.
D) The owner must pay double the equivalent wage.

Key Takeaway
In muzara'ah, the seed owner is excused from compulsion due to risk; if he refuses after plowing, he owes a conscience wage but not a court-enforceable wage.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
advanced
10 min
Termination of Muzara'ah by Death and Related Issues
Commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq: rulings on termination by death, debt, and sale of land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on termination of muzara'ah by death of a party, distinguishing between qiyas and istihsan, and apply it to scenarios involving debt and sale of land.

Core Idea
By qiyas, muzara'ah terminates at death; by istihsan, if the crop has grown, the contract continues until harvest to protect both parties.

Muzara'ah is considered a lease (ijarah), and leases generally terminate with the death of a party. However, Hanafi jurists applied istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the contract if the crop has already grown. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, along with related issues: the effect of debt forcing a sale of the land, and the need for a judge's decree in rescission.

Guided Path
1
State the qiyas ruling
By analogy to ijarah, muzara'ah becomes void upon the death of either party because the contract is personal.
2
Introduce the istihsan exception
If the crop has grown (naba al-zar'), the contract remains valid until the crop is harvested to respect both parties' rights. This is istihsan.
Reason: premature termination would waste the crop and harm both.
3
Apply to scenarios before planting and after planting
If death occurs before planting, the contract ends with no liability. If after planting but before growth, there is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars.
4
Analyze the impact of debt on the land
If the landowner dies with debt, the land may be sold. If the crop has not yet grown, the sale is allowed and the worker is not compensated for plowing. If the crop has grown, sale is postponed until harvest to protect the worker's right.
5
Evaluate the need for a judge's decree in rescission
There is a difference within the school: some narrations require a judge's decree or mutual consent to rescind, others do not.

قال رحمه الله : (فإن لم يخرج شيء فلا شيء للعامل لأنها إما اجاره أو شركة، فإن كانت اجارة فالواجب في العقد الصحيح منها المسمى وهو معدوم فلا يستحق غيره، وإن كانت شركة فالشركة في الخارج دون غيره فلا يستحق لم بيع الأرض بالدين حتى يستحصد الزرع لأن في البيع إبطال حق المزارع والتأخير أهون من الإبطال ويخرجه القاضي من الحبس إن كان حبسه به لأنه لم يمنع بيع الأرض لم يكن مماطلاً والحبس جزاء المماطلة وفي الذخيرة ولو مات رب الأرض بعد الزرع قبل النبات هل تبقى المزارعة ؟ قال بعضهم تبقى. وقال بعضهم لا تبقى فتفسخ . وفيها أيضاً: وهل يحتاج في فسخ المزارعة إلى قضاء القاضي؟ قيل : وفي رواية الزيادات يحتاج إل القضاء والرضا، وفي رواية كتاب المزارعة لا يحتاج إلى القضاء أو الرضا اهـ. ولو مات
Book of Muzara'ah. So the produce is according to the condition, and if nothing comes out then nothing for the worker. And whoever refuses to proceed is compelled except for the straw? It is valid because it is the intended purpose, and the straw is half each. And if they stipulate the grain half and the figs for the owner of the land, it is valid because it is a condition that does not contradict the contract because it is the growth of his property. And if they stipulate the straw for the worker, it is corrupt because it is a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract, and maybe it leads to cutting the partnership by a blight afflicting the crop so the grain does not form and only straw comes out. He said: And the tithe is upon both according to them, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa upon the owner of the land. If the imam does not take the tithe, then it belongs to the owner of the land according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to them it belongs to both. And if the owner of the land says to the worker: I do not know what the imam will take, the tithe or half, because the half is for me after he takes, it is valid according to them. Likewise in al-Muhit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If it is valid, then the produce is according to the condition due to the validity of the commitment.) He said in al-Muhit: As for increase and decrease in muzara'ah and mu'amalah, the best is if the contracted thing is in a state that allows the initiation of muzara'ah and mu'amalah, then increase in them is permissible. And if one of them gives the other in the produce, if the increase is before harvest and the crop has reached its full growth, increase is permissible because the initiation of the contract is permissible as long as it is capable of increase, otherwise not. And decrease is permissible in both cases, the case of accepting increase and after it, because it is a relinquishment. And if he sells the land given in muzara'ah or mu'amalah, the sale is suspended pending the permission of the muzari' and the worker. If he permits, it remains until the end of the muzara'ah and mu'amalah, and the buyer is given the choice: if he wishes he waits or rescinds. The author did not address when the contract is contingent or conditioned, and we will explain that. He said, and also in it: If he gives the land and seed for a year on condition that he cultivates it without plowing, then for the worker a quarter of the produce; if he plows it, then a third; if he plows and builds, then half; whatever they stipulate is valid. Likewise if the seed is from the muzari'. The second section: giving the land on condition that he cultivates it with wheat, then the produce is such; if he cultivates it with barley, then such; if with sesame, then such. So this is in four aspects: If he says 'cultivate it' or 'you cultivated in it' or 'you cultivated from it' or 'you cultivated some of it', then the muzara'ah in the first two is valid because he gave him a choice between three contracts. If he cultivates something from the three varieties, then the produce is according to what they stipulated. And if he says 'what you cultivated from it' or 'some of it', then the muzara'ah is corrupt because if he cultivates some wheat, some barley, and some sesame, then that part is unknown. And if the seed is from the worker and he stipulates that if he cultivates it with wheat then between them half, and if he cultivates it with barley then that is for the worker, it is valid by istihsan. The first is muzara'ah and the second is loan of land. Then Muhammad mentioned choice among three, but did not mention whether choice is permissible in more than that? Hisham narrated that it is not permissible. Third section: giving the land on condition that he cultivate it with his seed in the first of Jumada al-Ula, then the produce is half, and if he delays then a third for the muzari'. Both conditions are valid according to them, and the explanation of the proof is sought therein. End. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If nothing comes out, then nothing for the worker) because it is either a lease or a partnership. If it is a lease, then the obligatory in a valid contract is the specified [wage], and it is nonexistent so he is not entitled to anything else. If it is a partnership, then the partnership is in the produce only, so he is not entitled to anything else, unlike when the muzara'ah is corrupt and [the seed owner?] and it becomes void by the death of one of them. If the period passes and the crop has not ripened, then the cultivator must pay an equivalent wage for the land where the equivalent wage is due for the period, and the lack of produce does not prevent its obligation. He said in al-Inayah: And it is problematic with one who hires a specific piece of land, then the hired person does the work and the land is destroyed before delivery, then he must pay the equivalent rent. So this should be similar because the muzara'ah was valid and the specified wage was lost. And it was answered that here the wage was lost after delivery because the muzari' took possession of the seed from which the produce branches, and possession of the origin is possession of its branches. And the other specific [wage] is not owed, so here too. And one may say: This answer is not correct in the case of hiring land, because the owner of the land does not take possession of the seed from which the produce branches so that his possession is possession of its branches. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And whoever refuses to proceed is compelled except the owner of the seed) because it is concluded as a lease, and lease is a binding contract, but it is dissolved due to an excuse. If the owner of the seed refuses to proceed, he is excused because he cannot proceed except by destroying his property, which is throwing the seed on the land, and he does not know if it will come out or not, so it becomes similar to if he hired him to demolish his house and then refused. And if the worker refuses, he is compelled to work. And if the owner of the seed and the land refuses after he has plowed the land, then there is nothing for him for the work of plowing in the court because his work is only valued by the contract, and he has forfeited it by [taking] a part of the produce, and there is no produce, and he must in what is between him and Allah the Exalted pay an equivalent wage for it, so that he is not deceived by him. Because he is harmed by it and he is repelled, so he is content by paying him his equivalent wage. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it becomes void by the death of one of them) because it is a lease, and a lease becomes void by the death of one of the contracting parties if he contracted for himself, and we have explained it in the chapter of Ijarah. This absolute statement is the answer of qiyas, and by istihsan, if he dies and the crop has grown, the lease contract remains until the crop is harvested, then it becomes void in the remainder. Because in keeping it for this period is consideration of both rights. So the worker or his heir works accordingly, and when harvested, they divide according to what they stipulated, and there is no need in the remainder. And if the owner of the land dies before planting after plowing and digging canals, the muzara'ah is rescinded because there is no destruction of the worker's property, and nothing for the worker in return for the work because it is valued by the produce and there is no produce. Nothing is owed, unlike the first case where he is compensated because he was deceived by his choice. And if the owner of the land has a debt and cannot pay it except by selling the land, then the muzara'ah is rescinded before planting and the land is sold for the debt, and nothing is owed to the worker for plowing and digging canals. And if the crop has grown but not harvested, the land is not sold for the debt until the crop is harvested because in selling there is nullification of the muzari's right, and delay is easier than nullification. And the judge releases him from prison if he was imprisoned for it because he did not prevent the sale of the land, he was not a dilatory, and imprisonment is the penalty for dilatoriness. And in al-Dhakhirah: If the owner of the land dies after planting but before growth, does the muzara'ah remain? Some said it remains. Some said it does not remain, so it is rescinded. And in it also: Is the rescission of muzara'ah in need of the judge's decree? It was said: And in the narration of al-Ziyadat, it needs the judge's decree and consent, and in the narration of the book of muzara'ah, it does not need the judge's decree or consent. End. And if he dies.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the rulings of muzara'ah (sharecropping) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author, Imam al-Mawsili, presents the matn statements and then expands them with reasoning, citations from other works (al-Muhit, al-Inayah, al-Dhakhirah), and intra-Hanafi discussions. The passage covers three main rulings: (1) distribution of produce and the condition that if nothing comes out, the worker gets nothing; (2) compulsion to proceed with the contract except for the owner of the seed; (3) termination of the contract by death of a party. The commentary uses qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) to derive and refine the rulings. For example, in the first ruling, the author explains that the contract is either a lease (ijara) or a partnership (shirkah), so if no produce comes out, the worker is not entitled to anything because the specified wage (in case of lease) is non-existent, or partnership is only in produce. There is an objection from al-Inayah comparing it to hiring land where the land is destroyed before delivery, but the author defends the ruling by arguing that the wage here is lost after delivery because the seed was taken possession of. In the second ruling, the owner of the seed is excused from being compelled because he cannot proceed without risking his property. The worker is compelled to work. If the owner of both seed and land refuses after plowing, he is not liable in court but must pay an equivalent wage in conscience to avoid deception. The third ruling states that the contract becomes void by death of either party by qiyas, but by istihsan, if the crop has grown, the contract remains until harvest to protect both parties' rights. The passage also includes details about increase and decrease in the contract, different scenarios of specifying crops, and the effect of debt on the land. The overall authority weight is from the commentaries of the later Hanafi scholars (al-Mawsili, etc.), building on the zahir al-riwayah of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling to avoid hardship.
النبات (al-nabāt): Crop growth; the stage after germination when plants are visible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
By istihsan, if the landowner dies after the crop has grown, what happens to the muzara'ah contract?
A) It becomes void immediately.
B) It continues until the crop is harvested.
C) It becomes a gift of the land to the worker.
D) The worker must vacate the land immediately.

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah terminates by death by qiyas, but by istihsan, if the crop has grown, the contract remains until harvest to protect both parties' rights.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Renting Property for Sinful Purposes: Prohibited Uses in Ijarah
Prohibits renting property for use as a fire temple, church, or for selling wine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on renting property for non-Muslim worship or wine selling and identify the rationale behind the prohibition.

Core Idea
A contract that facilitates sin is invalid—renting for places of worship or wine selling is haram.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on the limits of permissibility in rental contracts. The passage explicitly prohibits renting a house to be used as a fire temple, church, synagogue, or for selling wine. The principle is that any contract that assists in disobedience to Allah is itself invalid and sinful. Understanding this ruling helps us apply the maqasid (objectives) of preserving faith and preventing harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts
List the specific purposes mentioned in the text: being used as a fire temple (bayt nar), church (bi'a), synagogue (kanisa), or for selling wine.
These are all acts of disbelief or sin.
2
Determine the hukm level
The ruling is haram (prohibited). The contract itself is invalid (fasid) because its subject matter involves sin.
In Hanafi fiqh, a contract that facilitates haram is itself haram to enter.
3
Understand the rationale
Renting for these purposes aids and abets sin (i'ānah 'alā al-ma'siyah). The lessor becomes a participant in the sin by enabling it.
This is based on the Quranic principle: 'Do not cooperate in sin and aggression' (5:2).
4
Scope of the prohibition
The prohibition applies whether the tenant is Muslim or dhimmi, and regardless of location. The text mentions 'in the countryside' (bi al-sawād) but the ruling is general.
Some later Hanafi scholars limit it to places where non-Muslim worship is not tolerated, but the relied-upon view is the general prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإجارة بيت ليتخذ بيت نار أو بيعة أو كنيسة أو يباع فيه خمراً بالسواد) و حمل خمر الذمي بأجر وبيع بناء
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And renting a house to be taken as a fire temple, or a church, or a synagogue, or that wine is sold therein in the countryside) and transporting the dhimmi's wine for hire and selling a building.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is not permissible to rent a house for purposes of religious places of non-Muslims (fire temple, church, synagogue) or for selling wine. This is because renting for such purposes aids sin and disobedience. The passage also mentions transporting wine for a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) and selling a building for such purposes, though the commentary is truncated here. The general principle is that any contract that facilitates sin is prohibited.

Key Terms
بيت نار (bayt nar): Fire temple, place of worship for Zoroastrians/Magians.
بيعة (bi'a): Church (Christian place of worship).
كنيسة (kanisa): Synagogue (Jewish place of worship).
خمر (khamr): Wine/intoxicants; selling it or facilitating its sale is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on renting a house to be used as a church?
A) Permissible if the tenant is a dhimmi
B) Prohibited because it aids sin
C) Disliked but not haram
D) Permissible if the rent is fair

Key Takeaway
Renting property for the worship of non-Muslims or for selling wine is haram because it aids sin and invalidates the contract.

Leasing Property for Non-Muslim Worship: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on leasing property for non-Muslim worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on leasing property for non-Muslim worship and explain the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Ṣāḥibayn.

Core Idea
A lease is on the benefit, not the sin; the lessor is not liable for the lessee's misuse.

When a Muslim landlord leases his property to a non-Muslim who intends to use it as a church, fire temple, or wine shop, is the lease valid? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. This lesson unpacks their arguments, the Quranic proof, and the practical outcome of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: leasing a house in the countryside (sawād) for worship or wine sale is permissible (jā’iz).
The matn explicitly permits it in the countryside.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Ṣāḥibayn): such leases are disliked (makrūh).
They base their view on a Quranic prohibition of cooperating in sin.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Quranic verse cited: 'Do not cooperate in sin and transgression' (5:2). The Ṣāḥibayn argue that leasing for sinful purposes constitutes cooperation.
The verse is a primary textual proof (dalīl naqlī).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: the lease is on the permissible benefit of the house; sin is solely the lessee's free choice, so it cannot be attributed to the lessor. He compares it to selling a slave-girl to one who will misuse her.
This is an application of the principle that the contract is evaluated on its own object, not the lessee's future actions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the lease is fully valid and rent is lawful; under the Ṣāḥibayn it is makrūh tanzīhan (slightly disliked) but still valid? The text does not declare it invalid, so the contract likely remains valid but is discouraged.
The restriction to the countryside limits the scope of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإجارة بيت ليتخذ بيت نار أو بيعة أو كنيسة أو يباع فيه خمراً بالسواد) يعني جاز إجارة البيت لكافر ليتخذ معبداً أو بيت نار للمجوس أو يباع فيه خمراً في السواد وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : يكره كل ذلك لقوله تعالى وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى ولا تعاونوا على الاثم والعدوان [المائدة: ٢] وله أن الإجارة على منفعة البيت ولهذا تجب الأجرة بمجرد التسليم ولا معصية فيه، وإنما المعصية بفعل المستأجر وهو مختار فيه فقطع نسبة ذلك إلى المؤجر وصار كبيع الجارية لمن لا يستبرئها أو يأتيها في دبرهـ دبرها أو بيع الغلام ممن يلوط به، والدليل عليه أنه لو أجره للسكنى جاز ولا بد فيه من عبادته وإنما قيده بالسواد لأنهم لا يمكنون من ذلك في الأمصار ولا يمكنون من إظهار بيع الخمر والخنزير في الأمصار لظهور شعائر الإسلام فلا يعارض بظهور شعائر الكفر ؛ قالوا في هذا سواد الكوفة لأن غالب أهلها أهل ذمة وأما في غيرها فيها شعائر الإسلام ظاهرة فلا يمكنون فيها في الأصح. وفي التتارخانية: مسلم له امرأة من أهل الذمة ليس له أن يمنعها من شرب الخمر وله أن يمنعها من إدخال الخمر بيته ولا يجبرها على الغسل من الجناية. وفي كتاب الخراج لأبي يوسف : المسلم يأمر جاريته الكتابية بالغسل من الجنابة ويجبرها على ذلك قالوا: يجب أن تكون المرأة الكتابية على هذا القياس أيضاً قال القدوري في النصرانية تحت المسلم: لا تنصب في بيته وتصلي في بيته حيث شاءت، ومن سأل من أهل الذمة المسلم طريق البيعة لا له ينبغي أن يدله عليها ا هـ.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And leasing a house to be taken as a fire temple, or a Jewish or Christian church, or for selling wine in it in the countryside (sawād)). Meaning: It is permissible to lease the house to a disbeliever to take it as a place of worship, or a fire temple for the Magians, or for selling wine in it in the countryside. This is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: All of that is disliked (makrūh) due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety, and do not cooperate in sin and transgression' (5:2). And for him (Abu Hanifa) is that the lease is on the benefit of the house, and for this reason the rent becomes obligatory upon mere delivery, and there is no sin in it. Instead, sin is by the action of the lessee, and he is free in his choice, so attribution of that to the lessor is cut off. It becomes like selling a slave-girl to one who will not perform istibrā' or will have anal intercourse with her, or selling a boy to one who will sodomize him. The proof of it is that if he leased it for residence, it would be permissible, and his worship is inevitable in it. He restricted it to the countryside (sawād) because they are not allowed to do that in the major cities (amṣār), nor are they allowed to display the sale of wine and pork in the cities due to the prominence of Islamic symbols, so they are not opposed by the appearance of symbols of disbelief. They said: In this, (it refers to) the countryside of Kufa because most of its people are dhimmis. As for other regions, Islamic symbols are apparent, so they are not permitted to do that in the most correct view. In al-Tātārkhāniyya: A Muslim who has a wife from the people of the dhimma is not allowed to prevent her from drinking wine, but he may prevent her from bringing wine into his house, and he does not force her to perform ghusl from janāba. In Kitāb al-Kharāj of Abu Yusuf: A Muslim may order his Christian slave-girl to perform ghusl from janāba and forces her to do so. They said: The Christian woman should be by this analogy as well. Al-Qudūrī said regarding a Christian woman under a Muslim: She does not set up a cross in his house and prays in his house wherever she wishes. If a person from the dhimmis asks a Muslim for the way to the church, it is not befitting for him to show it to him.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (within Hanafi school) regarding leasing a house to a non-Muslim for religious worship or selling wine. The matn (from Kanz al-Daqā’iq) permits it but only in the countryside (sawād). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the lease is on the benefit of the house, which is permissible, and sin is solely the act of the lessee. Therefore, the lessor is not assisting in sin. He compares it to selling a slave-girl to someone who will misuse her—the seller is not accountable for future acts. The Ṣāḥibayn argue that such a lease is disliked (makrūh) based on the Quranic verse prohibiting cooperation in sin. They see the lease as enabling sinful acts. The text notes the restriction to the countryside (sawād) because in major Islamic cities, non-Muslims cannot openly practice their rites or sell wine, so the issue does not arise. It then digresses into related rules: a Muslim husband cannot stop his Christian wife from drinking wine but can stop her from bringing it home; he does not force her to bathe from janāba. Abu Yusuf's book allows forcing a Christian slave-girl to perform ghusl. Al-Qudūrī adds that a Christian wife should not set up a cross in the Muslim's house but may pray there. Additionally, a Muslim should not show a dhimmi the way to a church.

Key Terms
السواد (al-sawād): The countryside, specifically the rural areas around Kufa where dhimmis were numerous.
البيعة (al-bī‘ah): A Jewish house of worship; sometimes used for church as well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is leasing a house to a non-Muslim for a church permissible?
A) Because the house is not used for sin.
B) Because sin is attributed to the lessee, not the lessor.
C) Because non-Muslims are allowed to worship freely.
D) Because the Quran permits it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits leasing property for non-Muslim worship only in the countryside (sawād); in cities, it is not allowed, reflecting a balance between contract freedom and Islamic public order.

Renting to Non-Muslims: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Permissibility and the Sawad Condition
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on renting property to non-Muslims for religious purposes in rural areas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on renting property to non-Muslims for worship or wine sale, explain Abu Hanifa's rational proof, and apply the condition of Sawad vs. Amsar.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits renting to non-Muslims in rural areas because the contract is on the benefit, not the sin; the lessee's independent act severs attribution.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a Muslim landlord may rent property to a non-Muslim for use as a place of worship or for selling wine. Imam Abu Hanifa deems it permissible, while his two students consider it disliked. The key factor is the location: rural areas (Sawad) versus cities where Islamic symbols dominate. We will unpack the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is renting a house to a non-Muslim (dhimmi) for them to use as a place of worship (church, fire-temple) or for selling wine. Two positions exist: Abu Hanifa says it is permissible; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is disliked.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the contract of hire is on the benefit of the house itself. The rent is due upon delivery, and the lessor has no control over the lessee's independent actions. The lessee's sin is not attributable to the lessor. Analogies: selling a slave-girl to someone who may not observe istibra' or who commits anal intercourse – the seller is not sinful because the buyer's misuse is separate.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of the contract.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's Objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad cite Quran 5:2: 'Do not help one another in sin and transgression.' They argue that enabling a non-Muslim to openly commit sinful acts (worship other than Islam, selling wine) constitutes cooperation in sin.
Quran 5:2 is their primary evidence.
4
Apply the Sawad vs. Amsar Condition
Abu Hanifa restricts the permissibility to the Sawad (rural areas), such as the Sawad of Kufa where the majority are dhimmis. In cities (Amsar), Islamic symbols are dominant, and dhimmis are not allowed to display their practices openly. Therefore, the ruling changes in cities: such rentals are not allowed.
This condition ensures that the lessor is not seen as subverting Islamic dominance.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view of permissibility with the Sawad condition. Ibn Nujaym in Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents it as the accepted view.
Intra-school conflict resolved by preferring the Imam's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعني جاز إجارة البيت لكافر ليتخذ معبداً أو بيت نار للمجوس أو يباع فيه خمراً في السواد وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : يكره كل ذلك لقوله تعالى وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى ولا تعاونوا على الاثم والعدوان [المائدة: 2] وله أن الإجارة على منفعة البيت ولهذا تجب الأجرة بمجرد التسليم ولا معصية فيه، وإنما المعصية بفعل المستأجر وهو مختار فيه فقطع نسبة ذلك إلى المؤجر وصار كبيع الجارية لمن لا يستبرئها أو يأتيها في دبرها أو بيع الغلام ممن يلوط به، والدليل عليه أنه لو أجره للسكنى جاز ولا بد فيه من عبادته وإنما قيده بالسواد لأنهم لا يمكنون من ذلك في الأمصار ولا يمكنون من إظهار بيع الخمر والخنزير في الأمصار لظهور شعائر الإسلام فلا يعارض بظهور شعائر الكفر ؛ قالوا في هذا سواد الكوفة لأن غالب أهلها أهل ذمة وأما في غيرها فيها شعائر الإسلام ظاهرة فلا يمكنون فيها في الأصح.
Meaning: It is permissible to rent a house to a disbeliever to take it as a place of worship or a fire-temple for the Magians or for wine to be sold in it in the Sawad (rural area). This is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: All that is disliked due to Allah's saying: 'Help one another in righteousness and piety, and do not help one another in sin and transgression' [5:2]. For him (Abu Hanifa) is that the contract of hire is upon the benefit of the house, and for this reason the rent is due upon mere delivery, and there is no disobedience in it; rather disobedience is by the act of the lessee, and he is independent in it, so the attribution of that to the lessor is severed, and it becomes like selling a slave-girl to one who will not observe her waiting period or will have anal intercourse with her, or selling a boy to one who will commit sodomy with him. The evidence for it is that if he rented it for dwelling it would be permissible, and there is inevitably in that (dwelling) his worship. He only restricted it to the Sawad because they are not allowed that in the cities, and they are not allowed to display the sale of wine and pigs in cities due to the manifest symbols of Islam, so it is not opposed by the manifest symbols of disbelief. They said: This applies to the Sawad of Kufa because most of its inhabitants are dhimmis; as for other (areas), the symbols of Islam are manifest there, so they are not allowed it in the most correct view.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of renting property to a non-Muslim for religious or prohibited purposes. The ruling begins by stating the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: it is permissible to rent a house to a disbeliever for use as a place of worship, a fire-temple for Magians, or for selling wine, provided this occurs in the Sawad (rural or non-urban areas). The author emphasizes that this is the view of Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, considering such rentals disliked (makruh) based on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:2) which prohibits cooperation in sin and transgression. They argue that enabling such activities constitutes cooperation in sin. Abu Hanifa's proof is rational: the contract of hire is validly concluded on the benefit of the house itself, and the lessor receives rent merely for granting possession; the lessee's independent sinful acts are not attributable to the lessor. The author illustrates this with analogies: selling a slave-girl to someone who may not observe istibra' or who may engage in anal intercourse, or selling a boy to a pederast – the seller is not sinful because the buyer's misuse is separate. Further, renting for dwelling is permissible even if the tenant engages in worship, which shows that the lessor is not responsible for the lessee's acts. The restriction to the Sawad is because in cities the symbols of Islam are dominant and non-Muslims are not permitted to openly display their practices, so the ruling differs. The commentator clarifies that this Sawad refers specifically to the Sawad of Kufa, as its population was predominantly dhimmi, but in other areas, Islam is dominant and dhimmis are restricted.

Key Terms
السواد (al-sawad): Rural or agricultural areas, specifically the Sawad of Kufa which was predominantly inhabitated by dhimmis.
شعائر الإسلام (sha'a'ir al-Islam): The outward symbols and practices of Islam, such as the call to prayer, mosques, and public observance of Islamic law.
المعصية (al-ma'siyah): Sin or disobedience to Allah; here it refers to the lessee's act of using the property for prohibited activities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, in which location is it permissible to rent a house to a non-Muslim for use as a church?
A) In any city (amsar) where Muslims are many.
B) In the Sawad of Kufa where most inhabitants are dhimmis.
C) In any area where the dhimmi pays jizya.
D) Only in non-Muslim countries.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits renting to non-Muslims in rural areas because the contract is on the benefit; the lessee's sin is independent and does not taint the contract, but this permissibility is conditioned on the location being in the Sawad not in cities.

Who May Hire Out a Minor? Mother’s Authority and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Ruling on hiring out a minor by mother or finder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on hiring out a minor, identify the conditions for validity, and distinguish between the narrations of al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Quduri.

Core Idea
A minor may be hired out only by his mother, but if the finder does so, it is also valid according to the closer view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on hiring out a minor child. The matn states that only the mother may hire him out. The commentary expands on this, citing two narrations within the Hanafi school: one restricts hiring to the mother, the other allows the finder. The text also addresses the case where the minor hires himself and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the mother's authority when the child is in the uncle's custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from the matn
The matn says 'his mother alone hires him out.' So the basic rule: only the mother may contract on behalf of the minor.
2
Note the two narrations
Al-Jami' al-Saghir restricts hiring to the mother. Al-Quduri allows the finder to hire him out to a craft. The author considers al-Quduri's narration 'closer.'
The finder (multaqit) is one who finds the child.
3
Examine the exception for the minor hiring himself
It is not valid because of potential harm, but if the work is completed, it becomes pure benefit and the wage is due. This is analogous to a restricted slave.
The analogy (qiyas) to the restricted slave (al-'abd al-mahjur) is used.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the child is with the uncle, Abu Hanifa says mother may still hire; Muhammad says no. The author implies the dispute is about who has custody and authority.
The text says 'الحفظ من' which may mean protection from harm.
5
Understand the legal reasoning
Contracts involving potential harm are invalid in principle, but valid post-facto if no harm remains. The benefit (manfa'ah) must be specified and lawful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتؤجره أمه فقط معناه أن الصغير لا يؤجره أحد من هؤلاء الثلاثة إلا الأم فإنها تؤجره إذا كان في حجرها ولا يملكه هؤلاء وهي رواية الجامع الصغير. وفي رواية القدوري : يجوز أن يؤجره الملتقط ويسلمه في صناعة فجعله من النوع الأول وهذا أقرب، فلو أجر الصبي نفسه لا يجوز لأنه مشوب بالضرر إلا إذا فرغ من العمل لأنه نفع محض بعد الفراغ فيجب المسمى وهو نظير العبد المحجور إذا أجر نفسه وقد ذكرناه من قبل، فإن كان الصغير في يد العم فأجرته أمه يجوز لأنه الحفظ من وهو قول أبي . وقال محمد : لا يجوز ا هـ . والله تعالى أعلم. يوم
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And his mother alone hires him out.' Its meaning is that none of these three hires out the minor except the mother; she hires him out if he is in her care, and others do not have that right. This is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir. In the narration of al-Quduri: It is permissible for the finder to hire him out and hand him over to a craft, making it of the first type, and this is closer. If the minor hires himself out, it is not permissible because it involves harm, unless he has completed the work, because it is pure benefit after completion, so the specified wage is obligatory. This is analogous to the restricted slave if he hires himself out, as we have mentioned before. If the minor is in the custody of the paternal uncle, and his mother hires him out, it is permissible because it is [protection from?] — and this is the statement of Abu Hanifa. Muhammad said: It is not permissible. End. And Allah knows best. Day.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage addresses the hiring out of a minor child. The matn states that only the mother may hire out the minor. The commentary clarifies that according to the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, none of the three guardians (uncle, mother, finder) may hire out the minor except the mother, if the child is in her care. However, according to the narration of al-Quduri, even the finder may hire out the minor to a craft, considering it a pure benefit (first type). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq considers this narration closer. The text then distinguishes: a minor hiring himself out is not valid because it involves potential harm, unless he has already completed the work, in which case it is a pure benefit and he is entitled to the wage, analogous to a restricted slave. Finally, if the minor is in the uncle's custody and the mother hires him out, Abu Hanifa permits it for the child's protection, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) does not.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A compilation of Hanafi rulings by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; this narration restricts hiring out to the mother.
القدوري (al-Quduri): A Hanafi scholar (Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri); his narration allows the finder to hire out the minor to a craft.
العبد المحجور (al-'abd al-mahjur): A restricted slave who is not permitted to engage in financial transactions without permission; analogous to a minor hiring himself out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, who may hire out a minor?
A) The father only.
B) The mother only.
C) The finder.
D) Any guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two narrations on hiring out a minor: one restricts to the mother, the other allows the finder; the closer view allows the finder, and the mother's authority is upheld by Abu Hanifa even when the child is with the uncle.

Hiring Out a Minor Child: Authority and Rulings
Ruling on hiring out a minor child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who has the authority to hire out a minor child in Hanafi fiqh, state the ruling when the minor hires himself, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Only the mother may hire out a minor in her custody; the minor's own hire is invalid unless work is completed.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the precise authority over hiring out a minor child. While many assume any guardian can act, the Hanafi school restricts this to the mother under specific conditions. We will examine the primary ruling, an alternative narration, an analogy to a constrained slave, and a dispute between the founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states that only the mother may hire out the minor child if he is under her care. This is based on the narration from Al-Jami' al-Saghir. Note that the father, grandfather, and executor are excluded.
This is the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Consider the alternative narration
Al-Quduri narrates that the finder (multaqat) of a foundling may also hire him out. This is presented as a closer view (aqrab), but it is not the primary ruling.
This shows there is some flexibility in the school.
3
Examine the minor hiring himself
If the minor hires himself out, the contract is invalid due to potential harm (gharar). However, if the work is completed, the wage becomes wajib because the benefit is realized. This is analogized (qiyas) to a constrained slave who hires himself.
The illa (effective cause) is the presence of harm initially, which is removed upon completion.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the minor is with his paternal uncle and the mother hires him out, Abu Hanifa permits it because she is the custodian. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan disagrees, ruling it invalid. The text sides with Abu Hanifa as the stronger view.
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether the mother's hire is valid despite the uncle's custody.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتؤجره أمه فقط ) معناه أن الصغير لا يؤجره أحد من هؤلاء الثلاثة إلا الأم فإنها تؤجره إذا كان في حجرها ولا يملكه هؤلاء وهي رواية الجامع الصغير. وفي رواية القدوري : يجوز أن يؤجره الملتقط ويسلمه في صناعة فجعله من النوع الأول وهذا أقرب، فلو أجر الصبي نفسه لا يجوز لأنه مشوب بالضرر إلا إذا فرغ من العمل لأنه نفع محض بعد الفراغ فيجب المسمى وهو نظير العبد المحجور إذا أجر نفسه وقد ذكرناه من قبل، فإن كان الصغير في يد العم فأجرته أمه يجوز لأنه الحفظ من وهو قول أبي حنيفة. وقال محمد : لا يجوز ا هـ . والله تعالى أعلم.
He (the author) said: 'And only his mother hires him out.' Its meaning is that no one among these three hires out the minor except the mother, for she hires him out if he is under her care, and these (others) do not have authority over him. This is the narration of Al-Jami' al-Saghir. In the narration of Al-Quduri: It is permissible for the finder (multaqat) to hire him out and hand him over to a trade, thus making it of the first type, and this is closer. If the minor hires himself out, it is not permissible because it involves harm, except if he has completed the work, because after completion it is pure benefit, so the named wage becomes obligatory. This is analogous to a constrained slave who hires himself out, as we have mentioned before. If the minor is under the care of the paternal uncle and his mother hires him out, it is permissible because she is the custodian. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa. Muhammad said: It is not permissible. End. And Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on hiring out a minor child. The author first states the decree: only the mother may hire out the minor when he is under her care; the other three (father, grandfather, or executor) cannot. This is based on the narration from Al-Jami' al-Saghir (a primary source in the Hanafi school). Then he presents another narration from Al-Quduri, which permits the finder (multaqat) to hire out a foundling and place him in a trade, considering this closer to the correct view. Next, he discusses the case where the minor hires himself: it is invalid because it involves potential harm, but if the work is already completed, the named wage becomes wajib (obligatory) since the benefit is now realized. This is analogized to a restrained slave who hires himself. Finally, a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan is noted: if the minor is with his paternal uncle, Abu Hanifa permits the mother to hire him out because she is the caretaker, while Muhammad does not allow it. The passage ends with 'Allah knows best.' The overall ruling is that the mother has the authority to hire out the minor when he is in her custody.

Key Terms
تؤجره (tu'jiruhu): She hires him out (i.e., rents his services to another).
ملتقط (multaqat): The finder of a lost child (foundling) who takes him in.
محجور (mahjur): Constrained or restricted slave (one who is not permitted to transact freely).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the primary narration in the text, who is allowed to hire out a minor child?
A) The father
B) The mother
C) The paternal uncle
D) The finder (multaqat) in all cases

Key Takeaway
The mother alone has the authority to hire out a minor in her custody; the minor's own hire is invalid until work is completed, and Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the dispute with Muhammad.

Lending the Pledge to the Mortgagor: Liability Ceases
Matn and commentary on lending the pledge to the owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the mortgagee's liability when he lends the pledge to the mortgagor and apply it to cases of loss.

Core Idea
Returning possession to the owner removes the mortgagee's liability.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies that when a mortgagee voluntarily returns the pledge to the mortgagor as a loan, the mortgagee's liability for the pledge ends. Additionally, a subsidiary ruling from al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya addresses the scenario where the debt is paid off and then the pledge perishes while still on loan to the mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key act
The mortgagee (murtahin) lends the pledged item (rahn) to the mortgagor (raahin). This is a contract of 'ariyah (gratuitous loan).
The pledge is returned temporarily, not permanently.
2
Understand the basis of liability
The mortgagee's liability (daman) for the pledge is based on his possession (qabd). He is responsible for loss while it is in his hands.
This is a known rule: al-daman bi al-qabd.
3
Analyze the effect of lending
By lending the pledge to the owner, the mortgagee voluntarily surrenders possession. Since liability was contingent on possession, it ceases. The pledge is no longer in his possession, so risk transfers back to the owner.
Even temporary return cancels liability.
4
Apply to the case of loss in the mortgagor's hand
If the pledge perishes while in the mortgagor's hand after the loan, the mortgagee bears no liability. The loss falls on the owner.
No compensation from mortgagee.
5
Note the exceptional ruling from al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya
If the mortgagor pays the debt and then the pledge perishes in the mortgagee's hand during the loan, the mortgagee must return the payment. This implies that after debt settlement, the mortgagee's holding becomes wrongful and he becomes liable.
This is a specific case from later fatwa literature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وخرج من باعارته من راهنه) يعني إذا أعار المرتهن الرهن من الراهن يخرج من ضمان المرتهن لأن الضمان كان باعتبار قبضه وقد انتقض بالرد إلى صاحبه فيرتفع بالضمان. قال رحمه الله : (ولو هلك في يد الراهن هلك مجاناً لارتفاع القبض الموجب للضمان على ما بيناه. وفي الفتاوى الغياثية : لو قضى الراهن دين المرتهن ثم هلك الرهن في العارية في يد المرتهن رد ما قبض.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it exits his liability by his lending it to the mortgagor) meaning if the mortgagee lends the pledge to the mortgagor, it exits the liability of the mortgagee because liability was based on possession and it has been nullified by returning it to its owner, so liability ceases. He said: (And if it perishes in the hand of the mortgagor, it perishes without compensation) because the possession that caused liability has been lifted. And in al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya: If the mortgagor pays off the debt of the mortgagee then the pledge perishes during the loan in the hand of the mortgagee, he may take back what he paid.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage addresses when the mortgagee (murtahin) lends the pledge (al-‘ariyah) to the mortgagor (raahin). The ruling is that the mortgagee's liability (daman) for the pledge ceases because liability was based on his possession, but by returning the pledge to its owner, that possession is nullified. If the pledge perishes in the mortgagor's hand while on loan, the loss is borne by the mortgagor without any compensation from the mortgagee. An additional ruling from al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya is cited: if the mortgagor pays the debt and then the pledge perishes in the hands of the mortgagee during the loan period, the mortgagee must return the amount he received. This shows that the surrender of possession is a temporary lifting of liability, but if the debt is settled, the return of the pledge becomes due.

Key Terms
إعارة (i'arh): Lending the pledge to the mortgagor, which temporarily removes the mortgagee's liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee lends the pledged item to the mortgagor and it perishes in the mortgagor's hand, who bears the loss?
A) The mortgagee, because he still holds the right of pledge.
B) The mortgagor, without any compensation from the mortgagee.
C) The third party who borrowed it.
D) Both share the loss.

Key Takeaway
Lending the pledge to the owner removes the mortgagee's liability because liability is based on possession.

Borrowing a Garment to Pawn It: Milk al-Yad
Matn and commentary on pawning a borrowed item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a borrowed item can be used as a pledge in Hanafi fiqh and distinguish milk al-yad from milk al-ayn.

Core Idea
You can pawn a borrowed item because possession (milk al-yad) suffices for a pledge, separate from ownership.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical scenario: a person borrows a garment with the intent to use it as collateral for a loan. At first glance, one might think that only the owner can pawn an item. However, the Hanafi school, through the concept of milk al-yad, validates this transaction. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is borrowing a garment with the intention to use it as a pledge. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
2
Understand Milk al-Yad vs Milk al-Ayn
Milk al-yad (ownership of possession) is a separate legal construct from milk al-ayn (ownership of the substance). The borrower has permission to possess, thus has milk al-yad.
This distinction is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the Qiyas (Analogy)
The commentary draws an analogy to sale: in a sale, ownership can transfer while possession remains with the seller (e.g., sale with condition). Similarly, in a pledge, the mortgagee gets a possessory right without ownership.
4
Apply the Principle
Since the borrower is a volunteer in establishing milk al-yad for the mortgagee, the pledge is valid. The amount of the pledge (little or much) is covered as long as the borrower authorizes it.
5
Note the Broader Implication
This ruling demonstrates that the Hanafi school recognizes milk al-yad as a standalone legal basis for certain transactions, such as pledges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو استعار ثوباً ليرهنه صح لأنه متبرع بإثبات ملك اليد فيعتبر التبرع بإثبات ملك العين واليد ويجوز أن ينفصل ملك اليد عن ملك العين ثبوتاً للمرتهن كما ينفصل لحق البيع زوالاً لأن البيع يزيل الملك دون اليد فيكون رهناً بما رهنه قليلاً كان أو كثيراً حيث أطلق له قال في المبسوط مسائله على فصول : أحدها في كيفية الإعارة، والثاني في اختلافهما في الهلاك والنقصان والثالث في ضمانه بهما . .
He said: (And if one borrows a garment to pledge it, it is valid) because he is a volunteer by establishing ownership over the hand (possession), so the voluntary act of establishing ownership of the item and the hand is considered, and it is permissible for ownership of the hand to separate from ownership of the item in terms of establishment for the mortgagee, just as it separates for the sake of sale in terms of removal, because sale removes ownership without removing the hand. So it becomes a pledge for whatever amount he pledges it, whether little or much, when he allows it. He said in al-Mabsut: its issues are in sections: first, on the manner of borrowing; second, on their disagreement about destruction and decrease; third, on guarantee.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
The matn rules that if a person borrows a garment (e.g., from someone else) with the intention of using it as a pledge for a loan, it is valid. The reasoning is that the borrower is a volunteer (mutabarri') in establishing the right of possession (ownership of the hand) for the mortgagee, separate from the ownership of the item itself (which remains with the lender). This is analogous to the case of sale, where ownership of the item is transferred but the seller may retain possession (e.g., in a sale with condition). Thus, the pledge contract is valid even if the pawner does not own the item itself; he only needs to have the right to possess it. The pledge covers the amount of the loan, whether large or small, as long as the borrower authorizes it. The commentary references al-Mabsut of Imam al-Sarakhsi for a more detailed classification of the issues surrounding borrowing for pledge.

Key Terms
ملك اليد (milk al-yad): Ownership of possession, a legal construct separate from ownership of the item itself, allowing one to give the item as a pledge even if not the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it valid for a person to borrow a garment and then use it as a pledge?
A) Because the borrower becomes the owner of the garment.
B) Because the borrower has ownership of the hand (possession) separate from ownership of the item.
C) Because the lender permits it.
D) Because the pledge contract does not require ownership.

Key Takeaway
A borrowed item can be validly pawned because the pledge requires only milk al-yad, not milk al-ayn.
